134. **Task [Extended] - Volume removal fix: source-of-truth name templates** (v3.10.7): The Manage Volumes feature was operating on the pre-COMPOSE_PROJECT_NAME volume name pattern, leaving cache/home/workspace deletions silent no-ops; UI labels were similarly stale<br>
     **Result**: After the COMPOSE_PROJECT_NAME refactor (v3.10.5), per-user volumes are named `{compose_project}_jupyterlab_{username}_{suffix}` (e.g. `myproject_jupyterlab_alice.smith_cache`), but `volumes.py` still hardcoded the old `f'jupyterlab-{username}_{suffix}'` pattern at line 75 and the home.html label rendered `<code>jupyterlab-{{ user.name }}_{{ volume_suffix }}</code>` - the docker SDK threw `NotFound` on every delete, the handler caught it, logged "skipping", and returned a success-shaped response with `reset_volumes=[]`. Single source of truth: added `get_user_volume_name_templates(volumes_dict, compose_project)` to `stellars_hub/volumes.py` that returns `{suffix: name_template_with_{username}_placeholder}` derived directly from `DOCKER_SPAWNER_VOLUMES` keys, exported via `__init__.py`. Wired through `c.JupyterHub.template_vars` and `tornado_settings.stellars_config` so both UI and handler read from the same map. `ManageVolumesHandler.delete` now constructs the name as `templates[volume_type].replace('{username}', encode_username_for_docker(username))`. `home.html` line 229 swapped to `{{ user_volume_name_templates[volume_suffix].replace('{username}', user.name) }}`. `admin.html` modal gained the same `<code>` line per volume; since admins can target any user, the substitution happens in JS at modal-open time using `data-template` attributes. Both `manage-volumes-modal` and `admin-manage-volumes-modal` got `modal-lg` for the longer namespaced names. Verified: helper produces `myproject_jupyterlab_alice.smith_cache` for cache/alice.smith (matches on-disk). Files: `services/jupyterhub/stellars_hub/stellars_hub/volumes.py`, `__init__.py`, `handlers/volumes.py`, `config/jupyterhub_config.py`, `services/jupyterhub/html_templates_enhanced/home.html`, `admin.html`.

135. **Task [Extended] - Unify volume metadata under one USER_VOLUMES dict (description, mount, name pattern)** (v3.10.7): Per-suffix VOLUME_DESCRIPTIONS dict and the patterned DOCKER_SPAWNER_VOLUMES dict were two separate sources of truth that had to be cross-referenced at every UI loop and could drift independently<br>
     **Result**: Replaced the two-dict layout with a single master config in `config/jupyterhub_config.py`: `USER_VOLUMES = {pattern: {mount, description}}` keyed by the same volume-name pattern (with `{username}` placeholder) used on disk, mirroring the structured shape of `settings_dictionary.yml` for env vars (each entry's identity in the key, all metadata fields in the value). Everything downstream derives mechanically: `DOCKER_SPAWNER_VOLUMES = {**{p: d['mount'] for p, d in USER_VOLUMES.items()}, f"{cp}_shared": "/mnt/shared"}` flattens for the spawner and adds the shared volume; `user_volume_suffixes` and `user_volume_name_templates` reuse the existing helpers in `stellars_hub/volumes.py`; new `user_volumes_for_ui = [{suffix, name_template, description}]` is precomputed in pattern-insertion order for the modal loop. `VOLUME_DESCRIPTIONS` is gone - descriptions only ever live in `USER_VOLUMES`. `c.JupyterHub.template_vars` exposes `user_volumes` (the precomputed list) instead of the old `volume_descriptions` and `user_volume_name_templates` cross-reference. Both `home.html` and `admin.html` were rewritten to iterate the unified list: `{% for v in user_volumes %}<strong>{{ v.suffix }}</strong><code>{{ v.name_template.replace('{username}', user.name) }}</code><small>{{ v.description }}</small>{% endfor %}` - one loop, three direct field reads, no more `if volume_descriptions and volume_suffix in volume_descriptions` guard. The deletion handler in `stellars_hub/handlers/volumes.py` is unchanged (still consumes `user_volume_name_templates` from tornado_settings) because that derivation was already correct after entry 134; it now just sources from a leaner config. Verified end-to-end with a Python sim: USER_VOLUMES with three entries -> derived DOCKER_SPAWNER_VOLUMES has 4 keys (3 user + shared), suffixes `[home, workspace, cache]`, templates `{home: ...home, workspace: ...workspace, cache: ...cache}`, `user_volumes_for_ui` carries each suffix + full pattern + description in order. Files: `config/jupyterhub_config.py`, `services/jupyterhub/html_templates_enhanced/home.html`, `admin.html`.

136. **Task [Extended] - User-volume defaults externalised to YAML + operator overlay merger** (v3.10.7): Volume metadata (mount + description per suffix) was hardcoded in `jupyterhub_config.py`; operators had no way to add a new volume suffix without editing the platform image<br>
     **Result**: Volume defaults now live in `services/jupyterhub/conf/volumes_dictionary.yml` (suffix-keyed map of `{mount, description}`), baked into the image at `/srv/jupyterhub/volumes_dictionary.yml` via Dockerfile COPY. Operators supply an overlay YAML (same shape) at the path indicated by `JUPYTERHUB_USER_VOLUMES_DESCRIPTIONS_FILE` and mount it via `compose_override.yml`. New `load_merged_user_volumes(defaults_path, overrides_path, compose_project)` in `stellars_hub/volumes.py` does per-suffix per-field merge with operator winning on conflict, missing fields falling back to the default, and operator-only suffixes added verbatim; returns the pattern-keyed `USER_VOLUMES` dict the rest of the system already consumes. `jupyterhub_config.py` replaced its inline three-entry dict with a single call to the loader. `compose.yml` passes the new env var through to the hub container; `settings_dictionary.yml` registers it under "User Environment" so it surfaces on the admin Settings page. `Dockerfile.jupyterhub` adds the COPY line and an empty `ENV` default. New docs page `docs/user-volumes.md` walks operators through the volume name pattern, the platform defaults table, the merge rule, and two worked examples (full overlay with override + addition; minimal description-only overlay) plus a file-reference table pointing at the loader and the merged dict location. Verified end-to-end: defaults-only load returns the three default suffixes with full patterns; defaults + overlay (docs example: change `home` description, override `cache` mount, add `models` suffix) merges correctly per-field. Files: `services/jupyterhub/conf/volumes_dictionary.yml`, `services/jupyterhub/conf/settings_dictionary.yml`, `services/jupyterhub/Dockerfile.jupyterhub`, `services/jupyterhub/stellars_hub/stellars_hub/volumes.py`, `__init__.py`, `config/jupyterhub_config.py`, `compose.yml`, `docs/user-volumes.md`.

137. **Task [Extended] - Manage Volumes lists only existing volumes; UI matches on-disk names** (v3.10.7): Triggered by an admin trying to reset volumes for `bob.jones` and seeing nothing happen<br>
     **Result**: Two layered bugs surfaced in one report. First, the modal labels rendered the raw username (`myproject_jupyterlab_bob.jones_cache`) but Docker volumes use escapism-encoded names (`bob-2ejones`); the deletion handler was already using the encoded form so its `NotFound` log was correct, but the UI was showing names that never existed on disk. Second, bob.jones had simply never spawned a server - DockerSpawner creates per-user volumes lazily on first start, so there was nothing to reset. The handler returned a success-shaped response with `reset=[], failed=[3 not_found]` and the modal alerted "Successfully reset 0 volume(s)", reading as a broken delete. Ported `escapism.escape(name, escape_char='-').lower()` to JS as `encodeUsernameForDocker()` in both admin.html and home.html so labels always match disk. Added `GET /hub/api/users/{name}/manage-volumes` to `ManageVolumesHandler` (shares an auth + Docker-client helper with the existing DELETE) that iterates `user_volume_name_templates`, queries `docker.volumes.get()` per candidate, and returns only the volumes that actually exist (with suffix, full name, description). Both modals replaced their static `{% for v in user_volumes %}` block with a `<div id="X-volumes-list">` placeholder; on `show.bs.modal` the JS calls the GET endpoint and renders dynamic checkboxes for the volumes returned (server-side filtered, no client-side guessing), or an empty-state message ("No volumes exist for this user yet." / "No volumes exist yet (your server has never been started).") when the response is empty. Reset button stays disabled in the empty case. The "Warning: This action cannot be undone!" banner switched from `alert-danger` (red) to `alert-warning` (yellow) since it's not actually an error, just a heads-up. Settings dictionary exposes `user_volumes` to the handler so descriptions stay in sync with the YAML-driven defaults from entry 136. `tornado_settings.stellars_config.user_volumes` added. Files: `services/jupyterhub/stellars_hub/stellars_hub/handlers/volumes.py`, `config/jupyterhub_config.py`, `services/jupyterhub/html_templates_enhanced/admin.html`, `home.html`.

138. **Task - Hadolint SC2015 cleanup in Dockerfile manifest verification** (v3.10.7): CI hadolint flagged the dpkg verification loop introduced with the yq fix<br>
     **Result**: `dpkg -s "$pkg" >/dev/null 2>&1 && echo "  OK: $pkg" || { echo "  MISSING: $pkg"; exit 1; }` reads as if-then-else but isn't - if the success branch's `echo` had ever failed, the failure branch would have run anyway and aborted the build. Replaced with an explicit `if dpkg -s "$pkg" >/dev/null 2>&1; then echo OK; else echo MISSING; exit 1; fi`. Semantically equivalent for the success path, correct for the failure path, and shellcheck-clean. File: `services/jupyterhub/Dockerfile.jupyterhub`.

139. **Task - Dockerfile hadolint SC2086 + announce-echo convention** (v3.10.7): Two Dockerfile hygiene follow-ups<br>
     **Result**: (1) Hadolint flagged `apt install -y ${PKGS}` with SC2086 (unquoted variable). The word-splitting was intentional but POSIX `sh` in the heredoc has no arrays, so refactored to `yq eval '.packages[]' /apt-packages.yml > /tmp/pkglist; xargs --no-run-if-empty apt install -y < /tmp/pkglist` - splitting now happens inside xargs, no shell variable to mis-quote, and `--no-run-if-empty` is a second defence against silent no-op installs alongside the dpkg verify loop. (2) Restored the convention that every `RUN <<-EOF` heredoc starts with an announce-echo BEFORE `set -e`, so the message appears as the step header in `docker build --progress=plain` output. The yq-install block was missing the echo entirely; the manifest-install block had it but after `set -e`. Both now lead with `echo "installing X..."`. Custom-assets block already followed the convention. File: `services/jupyterhub/Dockerfile.jupyterhub`.

140. **Task [Extended] - Two-stage TLS cert provisioning: /mnt/user_certs overlay + /mnt/certs runtime** (v3.10.7): Operators previously had to rewrite Traefik's whole command line in compose_override.yml to ship custom certs; replaced with an in-image bootstrap that reads operator certs from a new mount and falls through cleanly when absent<br>
     **Result**: New `services/jupyterhub/conf/bin/start-platform.d/00_provision_certificates.sh` (replaces the older `00_generate_ssl_cert.sh`) implements a three-tier decision tree at hub startup: (1) operator-supplied - any `*.yml`/`*.yaml` under `/mnt/user_certs` whose every `certFile`/`keyFile`/`caFile` reference (extracted via `yq eval '.. | (.certFile? , .keyFile? , .caFile?) | select(. != null)'`, recursive descent through any nesting) resolves to an existing file under `/mnt/user_certs` - copy yml + cert/key into `/mnt/certs`, sed-rewrite `/mnt/user_certs/`->`/mnt/certs/` in the copied yml so paths stay self-consistent. All-or-nothing: a single missing reference rejects the whole operator path. (2) Persisted - `/mnt/certs` already has at least one `*.crt` + one `*.yml`/`*.yaml` from a prior boot - use as-is. (3) Auto-generate - call existing `mkcert.sh` for a 365-day self-signed CN=$CERTIFICATE_DOMAIN_NAME cert plus a default `certs.yml`. Status banner at end logs the source label (`operator-supplied` / `persisted` / `auto-generated`), every yml present, and per-cert subject / SAN / issuer / expiry via `openssl x509 -noout`. `compose.yml` declares a new top-level `jupyterhub_user_certs` volume (named `${COMPOSE_PROJECT_NAME}_user_certs`, read-only mount on the hub at `/mnt/user_certs`); operators bind-mount their cert dir over it via `compose_override.yml`: `- ../certs:/mnt/user_certs:ro` - no Traefik command surgery needed because Traefik already scans `/mnt/certs/` (directory provider, watch=true). `Dockerfile.jupyterhub` adds `ENV CERTIFICATE_USER_CERTS_DIR=/mnt/user_certs` for symmetry with the existing `CERTIFICATE_DOMAIN_NAME`. New `docs/certificates.md` walks operators through the scenario table, the override snippet, sample yml + cert layout, and the log banner format. Verified end-to-end via a six-scenario shell-sim harness (`reset_dirs` + `gen_pair` helpers driving every row of the scenario table) using mikefarah/yq v4.44.3: all six paths produce the correct source label and the correct files in target. Files: `services/jupyterhub/conf/bin/start-platform.d/00_provision_certificates.sh` (new), deleted `00_generate_ssl_cert.sh`, `compose.yml`, `services/jupyterhub/Dockerfile.jupyterhub`, `docs/certificates.md`.

141. **Task - Replace project.env with pyproject.toml (inline extraction)** (v3.10.8): Project metadata moved to PEP-621 layout; Makefile and build scripts read it inline via `python3 -c 'import tomllib; ...'` with no helper scripts<br>
     **Result**: `project.env` (11-line shell-syntax `KEY="value"`) deleted in favor of a minimal root `pyproject.toml`: `[project]` name/version/description/authors + `[tool.stellars]` cuda/jupyterhub. The image tag `3.10.8_cuda-13.0.2_jh-5.4.2` is composed at read time as `${version}_cuda-${cuda}_jh-${jupyterhub}`. Makefile uses single `$(shell python3 -c ...)` populating four `$(word ...)` extractions; `$(error ...)` guard fails parse-time if pyproject.toml is unreadable; new `REQUIRED_TOOLS` list + `check_versioning_deps` recipe (prereq of `increment_version`) verifies python3/awk/sed and tomllib at recipe time. `increment_version` rewrites pyproject.toml's `[project] version` patch via inline `awk -F.` + `sed -i`. `scripts/build.sh`, `scripts/build_verbose.sh`, and `.claude/commands/checkpoint.md` all switched to the same one-liner. `.claude/CLAUDE.md` updated. Verified: composed tag matches old project.env VERSION; `make -n rebuild` shows `--build-arg VERSION=3.10.8_cuda-13.0.2_jh-5.4.2`; `make help` unchanged. Files: `pyproject.toml` (new), deleted `project.env`, `Makefile`, `scripts/build.sh`, `scripts/build_verbose.sh`, `.claude/commands/checkpoint.md`, `.claude/CLAUDE.md`.

142. **Task [Extended] - Two-stage config provisioning: /mnt/user_config overlay + /srv/config runtime** (v3.10.8): Compose file becomes a standalone artefact - the image ships a working built-in `jupyterhub_config.py` and any operator overlay flows through a separate mount<br>
     **Result**: New `services/jupyterhub/conf/bin/start-platform.d/01_provision_config.sh` selects between `/mnt/user_config` (operator) and `/srv/jupyterhub/jupyterhub_config.py` (built-in), populating `/srv/config/` which JupyterHub now loads via `start-platform.sh`'s updated `-f /srv/config/jupyterhub_config.py`. Trigger is the presence of the root file (default `jupyterhub_config.py`, overridable via `JUPYTERHUB_USER_CONFIG_FILE`); missing root falls back silently to built-in, empty or syntactically broken root fails boot with `exit 1` so operator typos surface immediately. Syntax check uses in-memory `python3 -c 'compile(...)'` rather than `py_compile` to avoid `__pycache__` writes against the read-only operator bind-mount. Siblings (helpers, auth modules) copied alongside and importable via `PYTHONPATH=/srv/config`; server files at `/srv/jupyterhub/` are never touched. Script re-runs every boot, `/srv/config` wiped first so removed overlays don't linger. New `docs/configuration.md` and `services/jupyterhub/tests/test_provision_config.sh` (28 assertions across 11 scenarios) wired into `.github/workflows/docker-build.yml` as a parallel CI job alongside hadolint. Also rolled in a `pyproject.toml` description tweak (two-paragraph form using "the current version" so the text doesn't drift with each bump). Files: `services/jupyterhub/conf/bin/start-platform.d/01_provision_config.sh` (new), `services/jupyterhub/tests/test_provision_config.sh` (new), `docs/configuration.md` (new), `services/jupyterhub/conf/bin/start-platform.sh`, `services/jupyterhub/Dockerfile.jupyterhub`, `compose.yml`, `.github/workflows/docker-build.yml`, `pyproject.toml`.

143. **Task - /mnt/user_certs and /mnt/user_config switched to host bind mounts** (v3.10.8): Operator overlays now route through `./certs/` and `./config/` next to compose.yml rather than docker-managed named volumes<br>
     **Result**: Replaced `jupyterhub_user_certs:/mnt/user_certs:ro` and `jupyterhub_user_config:/mnt/user_config:ro` with `./certs:/mnt/user_certs:ro` and `./config:/mnt/user_config:ro` in upstream `compose.yml`; dropped both named-volume declarations. Resolution is relative to the base compose file's dir, so missing host folders cause docker to auto-create empty dirs which the provisioning scripts cleanly fall through (cert auto-gen self-signed, config built-in). Operators populate `./certs/` or `./config/` next to compose.yml to override - no compose changes needed; `compose_override.yml` still lets deployments point the binds at different host paths. `docs/certificates.md` and `docs/configuration.md` updated to describe the wired-in default. 145. **Task [Extended] - Makefile preflight + version-bump awk fix + rebuild target rename** (v3.10.8 -> v3.10.9): `make rebuild && make push` blew up because the awk version-bumper produced "3 10 9" (space-separated) instead of "3.10.9", which then got injected into the docker tag as a multi-arg buildx invocation; rolled in a broader Makefile cleanup<br>
     **Result**: Awk recipe `awk -F. '{$NF += 1; OFS="."; print}'` had a subtle ordering bug - `$NF += 1` rebuilds `$0` with the OLD OFS (space, the default) before the OFS reassignment takes effect, so the joined output used spaces. Fixed via `awk 'BEGIN{FS=OFS="."} {$NF += 1; print}'` which sets both at parse time before any field assignment. `pyproject.toml` was restored from the corrupted `version = "3 10 9"` to `version = "3.10.9"`. New `preflight` target replaces the narrower `check_versioning_deps` and reports OK/MISSING per item with column-aligned output covering `python3`/`awk`/`sed`/`bash`/`docker`/`git`, `python3 -c 'import tomllib'` (>=3.11 check), `docker compose version --short` (compose plugin), `docker info` (daemon reachable), and the three load-bearing project files (`pyproject.toml`, `compose.yml`, `services/jupyterhub/Dockerfile.jupyterhub`); exits 1 if any required item is absent. Wired as a hard prereq on every state-modifying target (`increment_version`, `build`, `build_verbose`, `rebuild`, `rebuild_no_increment`, `pull`, `push`, `tag`, `start`, `stop`, `logs`, `clean`); deliberately not on `help` so the help screen still works when the daemon is unreachable. Targets renamed per operator request: OLD `rebuild` (which increments + builds) is now `rebuild_increment_version`; OLD `rebuild_no_version_increment` (no increment) is now `rebuild`, the safer dev-iteration default. The actual docker build recipe was factored into a phony `_rebuild_impl` helper so both targets share it without recursion or sub-make overhead, with `$(eval CURRENT_VERSION := $(shell python3 -c '...'))` reading pyproject.toml at recipe time so any preceding `maybe_increment_version` bump is picked up. (An interim rename to `rebuild_no_increment` was a misread of the operator's instructions; corrected to `rebuild_increment_version` so the name matches the behaviour.) Files: `Makefile`, `pyproject.toml`.

146. **Task [Extended] - Buildkit ENV warnings + uv.lock hygiene + Makefile color banners** (v3.10.9): Three small Makefile / Dockerfile polish items rolled together<br>
     **Result**: (1) Buildkit's `SecretsUsedInArgOrEnv` check was firing on `JUPYTERHUB_AUTOGENERATED_PASSWORD_WORDS` and `_DELIMITER` ENV declarations because of a substring match on "PASSWORD" in the variable name - both are xkcdpass generation parameters (word count, delimiter), not credentials. Added the `# check=skip=SecretsUsedInArgOrEnv` parser directive at the top of `services/jupyterhub/Dockerfile.jupyterhub` plus a 3-line comment explaining why the skip is safe; verified with `docker build --check` ("Check complete, no warnings found"). (2) Removed a stray `uv.lock` from the repo root that had been accidentally committed in commit `5fa0918`; the root `pyproject.toml` is purely a project descriptor consumed by inline `python3 -c 'import tomllib'` extraction in the Makefile (no `[project.dependencies]`, no `[build-system]`), so a uv lockfile is never needed at this level. Added `/uv.lock` to `.gitignore` so the file does not sneak back in. (3) Added cyan/bold version-status banner ("Version bumped: 3.10.9 -> 3.10.10" or "Version unchanged: 3.10.9 (--no-version-increment)") on every increment / no-increment path, and a green/bold "Build successful: stellars/stellars-jupyterhub-ds:<tag>" banner at the end of `build`, `build_verbose`, and `_rebuild_impl`. Reusable `PRINT_BUILD_SUCCESS` macro reads pyproject.toml at recipe-shell time via `python3 -c 'import tomllib'` so any preceding bump is reflected in the printed tag. Colors come from `$(shell tput setaf N)` evaluated at parse time and degrade to empty strings on `dumb` terminals. Files: `services/jupyterhub/Dockerfile.jupyterhub`, `.gitignore`, deleted `uv.lock`, `Makefile`.

147. **Task - Banner expansion: push + preflight green/red, blank-line padding** (v3.10.9): Followed up entry 146 by extending the success-banner pattern to `push` and `preflight`, with blank-line padding around build banners<br>
     **Result**: New `PRINT_PUSH_SUCCESS` macro mirrors `PRINT_BUILD_SUCCESS` ("Push successful: stellars/stellars-jupyterhub-ds:<tag> (also :latest)") and is appended to the `push` recipe after the two `docker push` calls. Both build and push success printfs now wrap their message in `\n...\n\n` so the green banner is visually separated from any subsequent shell output. The python tag-reader was hoisted into a shared `RUNTIME_TAG_PYTHON_CMD := python3 -c '...'` variable so build and push macros share one definition. `preflight` got the same treatment - success line is now green/bold ("Preflight passed - all required tools, services, and files are available.") and failure is red/bold ("Preflight FAILED - install / start the missing items above.") via a new `RED := $(shell tput setaf 1)` colour var. 149. **Task [Extended] - Activity-monitor volume-size cache silently empty after COMPOSE_PROJECT_NAME refactor** (v3.10.9): Operator noticed the volume-size column on `/hub/activity` showed 0 MB for every user; same shape as entry 134's `Manage Volumes` silent-no-op bug<br>
     **Result**: `services/jupyterhub/stellars_hub/stellars_hub/volume_cache.py:_fetch_volume_sizes()` was filtering disk volumes by the pre-3.10.5 prefix `jupyterlab-` (literal startswith), but per-user volumes are now namespaced as `{compose_project}_jupyterlab_{username}_{suffix}` (e.g. `myproject_jupyterlab_alice-2esmith_cache`). Every modern volume failed the prefix check, so the cache stayed empty and the activity page rendered zeros. Verified against the live daemon: `docker volume ls` shows the namespaced format. Fixed by introducing `configure_volume_cache(templates)` which compiles each entry of `user_volume_name_templates` (e.g. `"myproject_jupyterlab_{username}_home"`) into an anchored regex with a capturing username group via `re.escape` + `replace(re.escape("{username}"), "(.+)")`. `_fetch_volume_sizes` now iterates regexes per disk volume, first match wins, captures encoded username + maps to suffix. Empty templates short-circuit to `{}` with a warning rather than producing stale cache. Wiring: `configure_volume_cache` exported from `stellars_hub/__init__.py`; `config/jupyterhub_config.py` calls it immediately after `user_volume_name_templates` is derived (before any handler runs), so the cache and `ManageVolumesHandler` read from the same single source of truth - future spawner naming changes only need touching `volumes.py:get_user_volume_name_templates()`. Added `services/jupyterhub/stellars_hub/tests/test_volume_cache.py` with six functional tests (default project, namespaced project, non-user volumes skipped, reconfigure replaces state, escapism-encoded usernames captured intact, empty config short-circuits). Verified end-to-end against real disk-volume names: 5 user volumes correctly matched and accumulated by encoded username; non-user volumes (`stellars_data`, `some_other_volume`) skipped. Total test count: 100 passing (was 94). Files: `services/jupyterhub/stellars_hub/stellars_hub/volume_cache.py`, `services/jupyterhub/stellars_hub/stellars_hub/__init__.py`, `config/jupyterhub_config.py`, `services/jupyterhub/stellars_hub/tests/test_volume_cache.py` (new).

150. **Task [Extended] - JupyterLab kernel-busy favicon override + redirect-loop fix** (v3.10.10): JupyterLab cycles `favicon-busy-{1,2,3}.ico` while a kernel runs; those requests were 302-looping (`?redirects=2`) through the hub, and there was no way to brand them<br>
     **Result**: The CHP favicon route registered in `hooks.py` covered the whole `/user/{username}/static/favicons/` directory and pointed it at the hub, but `handlers/favicon.py` only matched `favicon.ico` exactly - so every kernel-busy frame reached the hub, missed the handler, fell through to JupyterHub's user-redirect logic, and looped. Two-part fix. (1) Default behaviour: narrowed the per-user CHP route from the directory prefix to the exact `…/static/favicons/favicon.ico` so CHP longest-prefix-match sends only the idle frame to the hub; the busy frames now fall to the generic `/user/{username}/` route and are served by the user's own JupyterLab server (its stock busy frames) - killing the loop with no override needed. (2) Override: new `JUPYTERHUB_FAVICON_BUSY_URI` env (file:// or URL). `setup_branding` copies a `file://` busy icon to hub static as `favicon-busy.ico` and returns `favicon_busy_target` (`hub/static/favicon-busy.ico`, or the URL, or `''`); when set, `hooks.py` registers an additional `…/static/favicons/favicon-busy` CHP route and the Tornado handler (pattern broadened to capture the filename, `initialize(busy_target)`) 302s busy frames to the custom icon (base-url-prepended for the static path, used as-is for a URL). Behaviour matrix: both URIs empty -> all JupyterLab defaults; main set, busy empty -> custom idle + JupyterLab default busy; both set -> custom idle + custom busy. Wired through `config/jupyterhub_config.py` (env read, `setup_branding`, `make_pre_spawn_hook`, `schedule_startup_favicon_callback`), `Dockerfile.jupyterhub` (`ENV` default), `compose.yml` (passthrough), `settings_dictionary.yml` (Branding entry). Tests: extended `test_branding.py` (busy file:// copy, nonexistent, URL, empty - and the new `favicon_busy_target` key) and new `test_favicon.py` (6 handler cases: idle -> hub static, idle ignores busy target, busy -> static target with base-url prepend, busy -> URL, busy-without-target falls back to idle, root base-url). Full suite 110 passing (was 100). Requires image rebuild + container restart to take effect. Files: `services/jupyterhub/stellars_hub/stellars_hub/branding.py`, `handlers/favicon.py`, `hooks.py`, `config/jupyterhub_config.py`, `services/jupyterhub/Dockerfile.jupyterhub`, `compose.yml`, `services/jupyterhub/conf/settings_dictionary.yml`, `tests/test_branding.py`, `tests/test_favicon.py` (new).

151. **Task [Extended] - Per-group CPU limit (quota model, mirrors memory limit)** (v3.10.11): Added a per-group CPU cap alongside the existing memory cap, using Docker's CPU-quota model (`--cpus N` equivalent) rather than core-pinning<br>
     **Result**: Confirmed via the installed DockerSpawner source that `spawner.cpu_limit` is honoured natively - it sets `cpu_quota = int(cpu_limit * cpu_period)` (cpu_period 100ms), i.e. the `--cpus` bandwidth cap that floats across cores - so CPU mirrors memory field-for-field. Chose the quota model over `cpuset-cpus` pinning because pinning is host-specific (breaks on a box with fewer cores), doesn't resolve sensibly across groups (you'd union core sets, which expands access rather than capping), and is about isolation not fair-share. `groups_config.py` `default_config()` gains `cpu_limit_enabled`/`cpu_limit_cores`. `group_resolver.py` accumulates `cpu_limit_cores` with the same biggest-enabled-wins rule as memory (disabled group never un-caps; enabled+0 or invalid -> no cap -> `None`), returns the raw value. `handlers/groups.py` PUT parses `cpu_limit_enabled` (bool) + `cpu_limit_cores` (`max(0.0, round(c,1))`); `GroupsPageHandler` now passes `host_cpu_count=os.cpu_count()` to the template as the max-allowed hint. `hooks.py` applies `spawner.cpu_limit = float(max(1, math.ceil(cores)))` - per operator request it ceils to whole cores so a fractional cap never rounds down to a zero-core quota (Docker treats `cpu_quota=0` as unlimited), with a floor of 1 core whenever a cap is set; the `[Groups]` spawn log now includes the applied `cpu_limit`. `groups.html` gained a separate "CPU" section (own `fa-microchip` header below Memory) with an enable checkbox, a cores input (`step 0.1`, `max={{ host_cpu_count }}`), the hint "This host has N core(s) available.", a note that values round up to whole cores (min 1), enable/disable wiring, load/save JS, and a `CPU` features-column badge. New `tests/test_group_resolver.py` covers CPU resolution (no-cap, single, fractional preserved, biggest-wins, disabled-doesn't-uncap, enabled-zero, invalid ignored, only-matched-groups, plus CPU/memory independence) - the resolver had no test before. Full suite 120 passing (was 110). Requires image rebuild + container restart; the cap applies on each user's next spawn. Files: `services/jupyterhub/stellars_hub/stellars_hub/groups_config.py`, `group_resolver.py`, `hooks.py`, `handlers/groups.py`, `services/jupyterhub/html_templates_enhanced/groups.html`, `services/jupyterhub/stellars_hub/tests/test_group_resolver.py` (new).

152. **Task [Extended] - Optional swap-disable on the per-group memory quota** (v3.10.12): A memory quota left swap at Docker's default (memory-swap = 2x memory), so a memory cap actually allowed an equal amount of disk swap on top before OOM; added an opt-in hard cap<br>
     **Result**: By default the platform only set `spawner.mem_limit`, leaving swap at Docker's 2x default - on a cgroup v2 host with a swap device, `memory.swap.max` ends up equal to the memory limit, so a cap permitted roughly double the configured amount before the OOM killer fired. Added an optional "Disable swap (hard cap)" checkbox to the per-group Memory section. `groups_config.py` `default_config()` gains `mem_swap_disabled: False`. `group_resolver.py` now carries the swap policy alongside the memory cap: the flag travels with the winning (biggest) limit - the group that owns the largest `mem_limit_gb` also decides swap, using strict `>` so ties keep the higher-priority group; returns `mem_swap_disabled`. `handlers/groups.py` PUT parses `mem_swap_disabled` (bool). `hooks.py` applies it by pinning `spawner.extra_host_config['memswap_limit'] = mem_bytes` (equal to the memory limit -> total RAM+swap == RAM -> zero swap allowance, cgroup v2 `memory.swap.max=0`); pops the key when not disabled or no limit; spawn log gains `swap_off=`. `groups.html` added the checkbox under the GB input (gated on mem-limit-enabled, with help text "OOM-killed at the limit instead of spilling to disk swap"), plus enable/disable wiring and load/save JS. Resolution stays coherent: each group's memory policy (cap + swap) applies as a unit; a smaller group's swap-disable is ignored when a bigger group grants more memory with swap allowed. Five new resolver tests (default-off, flag-on, no-limit-off, swap-follows-bigger-limit both directions). Full suite 125 passing (was 120). Requires image rebuild + container restart; applies on each user's next spawn. Files: `services/jupyterhub/stellars_hub/stellars_hub/groups_config.py`, `group_resolver.py`, `hooks.py`, `handlers/groups.py`, `services/jupyterhub/html_templates_enhanced/groups.html`, `services/jupyterhub/stellars_hub/tests/test_group_resolver.py`.

155. **Task [Extended] - Session-extend replenish + real in-hub cull enforcement** (v3.10.12): Made the idle-culler session-extension actually delay culling, added opt-in replenish of elapsed idle time, and consolidated all the math into a new `stellars_hub.idle_culler` submodule<br>
     **Result**: Planning surfaced that extend was display-only - `ExtendSessionHandler` wrote `extension_hours_used` to `orm_spawner.state` and the UI read it back, but the cull ran as the stock `jupyterhub_idle_culler` service with a fixed `--timeout=base` that never reads spawner state (its per-server override at `__init__.py:225-237` is commented-out example code). The REST API also exposes `spawner.get_state()` not stored state (`apihandlers/base.py:192`), so an external culler couldn't see the extension without a `get_state` override plus `admin:server_state` scope. Chose in-hub enforcement: the repo already grabs the running app via `JupyterHub.instance()` and schedules IOLoop callbacks (`hooks.py`), so a periodic in-process pass reads `orm_spawner.state`/`last_activity` directly - same data the UI uses, one source of truth. New `idle_culler.py` holds the pure calcs (`calc_effective_timeout`, `calc_ceiling`, `calc_time_remaining` now ceiling-clamped, `calc_available_hours`, `calc_new_extensions` simplified to `current+hours`, `should_cull`) plus `run_cull_pass`/`schedule_idle_culler` (heavy imports inside the fns so the module stays stdlib-only at import for tests). Model: `remaining = clamp(effective-elapsed, 0, ceiling)`; offer = gap to ceiling (replenish + headroom); extend adds the chosen hours and may push `ext_used` beyond `max_extension` so already-elapsed idle is recoverable, while the clamp stops remaining ever displaying above the ceiling - fixing journal-317's balloon-on-activity-reset without re-capping at max_extension. `session.py` re-exports the calcs (back-compat) and clamps; `activity.py` clamps too; `services.py` dropped the external culler service/role; `config` schedules the in-hub culler when enabled; Dockerfile ENV defaults corrected to the `_MINUTES` names (leftover from the rename); desktop extend input max now tracks `available`. Removed `test_session.py`, added scenario-driven `test_idle_culler.py` (replenish flows, clamp, `should_cull` truth table, end-to-end timelines, re-export check); updated `test_services.py`/`test_imports.py` for the new signature. Full suite 138 passing. Repo-only - requires image rebuild to take effect. Files: `idle_culler.py` (new), `__init__.py`, `handlers/session.py`, `handlers/activity.py`, `services.py`, `config/jupyterhub_config.py`, `Dockerfile.jupyterhub`, `session-timer.js`, `README.md`, `tests/test_idle_culler.py` (new), `tests/test_services.py`, `tests/test_imports.py`, removed `tests/test_session.py`.

156. **Task [Extended] - GPU enumeration + per-group GPU selection** (v3.10.12): Added host-GPU enumeration via the existing ephemeral detection container and a per-group "all GPUs / specific GPUs" config with validation; created docs<br>
     **Result**: The hub has no GPU access of its own, so detection already runs nvidia-smi in an ephemeral runtime=nvidia CUDA container at startup. Consolidated detection + enumeration into that single run: new `enumerate_gpus()` in `gpu.py` runs `nvidia-smi --query-gpu=index,name,uuid,memory.total --format=csv,noheader`, parses stdout into `[{index,name,uuid,memory_mb}]`, returns `[]` on any failure (no GPU / runtime / docker error - never crashes). `detect_nvidia()` now derives from it (1 if list else 0) and `resolve_gpu_mode()` returns a 3-tuple `(gpu_enabled, nvidia_detected, gpu_list)`, enumerating in both forced (mode 1) and autodetect (mode 2); mode 0 spins nothing. `config/jupyterhub_config.py` unpacks the tuple, caches `gpu_list` into `stellars_config`, and prints a one-line startup `[GPU debug]`. Per-group feature: `groups_config.default_config()` gains `gpu_all` (default True) + `gpu_device_ids` (list) plus a pure `validate_gpu_selection()` (access on + not-all + no ids -> invalid). `group_resolver` collapses GPU across groups: access OR'd then gated on hardware, all-GPUs wins, otherwise device-ids unioned, empty-selection falls back to all. `hooks.py` builds `device_requests` with `Count:-1` for all or `DeviceIDs` for specific; gated on availability so a GPU-less host sets nothing and spawns never crash; spawn log adds `gpu_sel`. `handlers/groups.py` PUT parses + validates the selection (400 on the incoherent state) and `GroupsPageHandler` passes the cached `gpus` to the template. `groups.html` GPU section: enable + "All GPUs" (default) checkboxes, per-GPU checkboxes revealed when all is deselected, whole section grayed-out with a "No GPUs detected" note when the host has none, client-side validation mirroring the server. 157. **Task [Extended] - GPU selection enforcement + WSL2 limitation findings** (v3.10.13): Investigated why a user assigned one GPU still saw all three; set `NVIDIA_VISIBLE_DEVICES` per selection and documented the platform-by-platform reality<br>
     **Result**: `docker inspect` of the user's container showed the device request was correct (`DeviceRequests=[{DeviceIDs:["2"]}]`) yet `nvidia-smi -L` listed all 3 GPUs. Root cause: the `stellars-jupyterlab-ds` image bakes `NVIDIA_VISIBLE_DEVICES=all`, and the NVIDIA Container Toolkit treats that env as the authoritative selector, overriding the Docker `DeviceIDs`. Deeper finding: the host is Docker Desktop on WSL2 (`docker.sock` under `docker-desktop-bind-mounts`, `HostConfig.Devices=null`), where GPUs are exposed through a single paravirtual `/dev/dxg` rather than per-GPU `/dev/nvidiaN` nodes - so per-GPU isolation is impossible there. Proven empirically: an ephemeral container with `NVIDIA_VISIBLE_DEVICES=<single-UUID>`, and `--gpus "device=2"` (which set `NVIDIA_VISIBLE_DEVICES=2` correctly in-container), both still showed all 3 GPUs; the container had only `/dev/dxg`, no `/dev/nvidia*`. On native Linux the toolkit injects only the allowed device nodes (cgroup denies the rest), so the same selection is true isolation. Fix: `hooks.py` now sets `spawner.environment['NVIDIA_VISIBLE_DEVICES']` per resolved selection (`all` / comma-joined ids / `void` for no-access) to override the image default; `NVIDIA_VISIBLE_DEVICES` added to `RESERVED_ENV_VAR_NAMES` so groups cannot set it. Net behaviour: specific selection enforced on native Linux, recorded-but-unenforced on WSL2 (the only WSL2 lever is the soft, app-level `CUDA_VISIBLE_DEVICES`, not set by the platform). New pure-information doc `docs/gpu-selection-jupyterlab-containers.md` (what we apply, host models, measured findings, enforcement matrix); `docs/gpu-detection-and-configuration.md` spawn section updated + cross-linked; memory `project-wsl2-gpu-no-partition` saved. 157 tests pass. `pyproject.toml` 3.10.12 -> 3.10.13 came from the operator's image rebuild and is committed here. Files: `hooks.py`, `config/jupyterhub_config.py`, `docs/gpu-selection-jupyterlab-containers.md` (new), `docs/gpu-detection-and-configuration.md`, `pyproject.toml`.

158. **Task [Extended] - CUDA_VISIBLE_DEVICES soft selection + WSL2 advisory in config UI** (v3.10.14): Web research confirmed WSL2 per-GPU isolation is unsupported; added a UUID-based CUDA_VISIBLE_DEVICES default and a WSL2 "advisory not a hard limit" notice on the Groups screen<br>
     **Result**: Verified on the live container that `NVIDIA_VISIBLE_DEVICES=2` is now applied (was `all`) yet `nvidia-smi -L` still lists all 3 GPUs - the host is Docker Desktop on WSL2 where GPUs come through one `/dev/dxg`. Web research (authorised) found NVIDIA's own [nvidia-container-toolkit #983] is the same symptom, stale/unfixed: per-GPU isolation is impossible on WSL2 (GPU-PV); GPU-P/DDA conflict with WSL2 GPU support; only native Linux gives true isolation. Per operator decision, added `CUDA_VISIBLE_DEVICES` alongside `NVIDIA_VISIBLE_DEVICES` in `hooks.py`: for a specific selection it is set to the chosen GPU **UUIDs** (not host indices - a selected GPU re-indexes to 0 in-container on native Linux, so indices would mis-target; UUIDs are order-independent and correct on both platforms), unset for all/no-access. The index->UUID map is built at startup (`GPU_UUID_BY_INDEX` from the enumeration) and passed to `make_pre_spawn_hook` via new `gpu_uuid_by_index` param. `CUDA_VISIBLE_DEVICES` added to `RESERVED_ENV_VAR_NAMES`. WSL2 detection: new `gpu.is_wsl2()` (kernel-string check) -> `GPU_ISOLATION_ENFORCED = has_gpus and not wsl2`, surfaced via `stellars_config['gpu_isolation_enforced']`; `GroupsPageHandler` passes it to the template and `groups.html` renders an amber "advisory, not a hard limit - containers can still reach all GPUs; CUDA defaults to the selection but is user-overridable" alert in the GPU section when false (true on native Linux -> no alert). Soft semantics throughout: `nvidia-smi`/gpustat still show all on WSL2 and a user can override `CUDA_VISIBLE_DEVICES`. Docs updated (`gpu-selection-jupyterlab-containers.md`, `gpu-detection-and-configuration.md`); memory `project-wsl2-gpu-no-partition` already records the constraint. 157 tests pass; `is_wsl2()` is True on this host so the advisory shows. `pyproject.toml` 3.10.13 -> 3.10.14 from the operator rebuild, committed here. Files: `gpu.py`, `hooks.py`, `config/jupyterhub_config.py`, `stellars_hub/__init__.py`, `handlers/groups.py`, `groups.html`, `docs/gpu-selection-jupyterlab-containers.md`, `docs/gpu-detection-and-configuration.md`, `pyproject.toml`.

159. **Task - Limited Docker access via owner-filtering socket proxy** (v3.10.14): Stop convenience-mess (one docker-sock user once made 250+ containers + 300 GB volumes); add a quota-bounded, per-user filtered Docker socket as a third orthogonal group grant; keep Docker Desktop simplicity<br>
     **Result**: Trigger: hygiene, not anti-hostile - one `docker-sock` user once spawned 250+ containers + 300 GB volumes. tecnativa `docker-socket-proxy` filters by API section only (no ownership); per-user DinD hides resources from Docker Desktop; Sysbox/AuthZ don't fit Docker Desktop. Modules: `filters` (label injection, name prefix, dangerous-flag rejection, compose-project scoping), `quota` (counts + `/system/df` per owner), `server` (`classify` -> mutate/guard/quota). `group_resolver` ORs grants, max-wins quotas, then **normal supersedes limited** (raw socket makes proxy moot). `docker_proxy.py`: `detect_self_image()` reuses hub tag as sidecar; `ensure_user_proxy()` launches per-user `jupyterlab-<base>-dockerproxy` with shared named volume; `hooks.py` sets `DOCKER_HOST=unix:///run/dockersock/docker.sock` so stock CLI works. `groups.html` enforces Normal/Limited XOR with quota panel. 161. **Task [Extended] - Dead-code GC round + `stellars_hub` -> `stellars_hub_services` rename** (v3.10.15): Operator-driven cleanup pass after the Docker work landed; safety checkpoint `CHECKPOINT_BEFORE_GC_3.10.15` (local) made the whole sweep revertable<br>
    **Result**: Two phases, one branch. **Phase 1 - GC**: spawned 5 parallel agents (general-purpose subagents) against a partitioned file checklist (`.claude/gc/CHECKLIST.md`); each owned a non-overlapping scope (core/hooks, groups+GPU+docker-proxy+idle-culler, activity+caches+volumes, handlers+templates+static, build+scripts+conf) and wrote findings to `.claude/gc/agent-N.md` with KEEP/PRUNE/DELETE/INCONCLUSIVE verdicts. Aggregate: 82 KEEP, 2 PRUNE, 0 DELETE, 3 cross-boundary flags. Per operator rule "aggressive pruning, if not used in production -> goes", the flags resolved as deletions: removed `stellars_hub/admin_bootstrap.py` entirely (every export shadowed by inline reimplementations in `config/jupyterhub_config.py` - inline is what production runs, module had zero callers); removed `stellars_hub/activity/sampler.py` entirely (superseded by `activity/service.py` as a JupyterHub managed service); pruned `helpers.py::record_activity_sample` (trivial wrapper, no prod caller) and `gpu.py::detect_nvidia` (thin wrapper over `enumerate_gpus`, not exported, no prod caller); dropped corresponding `__init__.py` re-exports + their `__all__` entries; dropped the 3 dead-symbol tests in `test_imports.py` and `test_gpu.py::TestDetectNvidia`; cleaned the 5 admin-bootstrap symbols from `config/jupyterhub_config.py`'s `from stellars_hub import (...)` block. 171 -> 168 stellars_hub tests (3 dead tests gone), 26 proxy tests untouched. **Phase 2 - rename**: operator asked for `stellars_hub` -> `stellars_hub_services` (Python module, underscored) and `stellars-hub` -> `stellars-hub-services` (project / pyproject `name`, dashed). 162. **Task [Extended] - Docker (root) fully orthogonal + sidecar log with limits + new docker-overview doc** (v3.10.16): Live triage of a user seeing every host container from their "limited" JupyterLab via `docker ps` exposed two issues: a missing quota-log signal at sidecar startup, and the validator forcing a within-group "root requires access" coupling that pushed operators into the legacy compound `docker-privileged` group (`docker_access=True` + `docker_privileged=True`), which the across-group "normal supersedes limited" rule then collapsed to raw socket whenever a user was also in `docker-limited`<br>
    **Result**: SQLite query against `/data/groups_config.sqlite` from the running hub confirmed it - the user was in both `docker-limited` and the legacy `docker-privileged`; resolver OR'd to (access=True, limited=True->False, privileged=True), so the bonanza was granted instead of limited+root. Three changes. (1) `docker_proxy.py::ensure_user_proxy` log lines now carry the resolved quotas/caps on both paths: `started docker-proxy sidecar ... limits: containers=N volumes=N networks=N storage_gb=N cpu=N mem_gb=N compose_project=X network=Y` on fresh launch, and `reused docker-proxy sidecar ... (limits unchanged: ...)` on idempotent reuse - operator can now `docker logs jupyterhub | grep docker-proxy` to confirm what the user is bounded by, and the "unchanged" marker makes it explicit that editing group quotas does not propagate to a running sidecar (needs `stop_user_proxy` + respawn). (2) Relaxed `validate_docker_selection`: dropped the "root requires access" branch - `docker_privileged` is now fully orthogonal. Standalone in a group it grants `--privileged` with no Docker socket (hooks.py already applied the flag orthogonally to the socket-mount branch, so no spawn-hook change needed). Operators can now create a pure `docker-root` group and combine it freely with `docker-access` or `docker-limited` from another group, sidestepping the legacy-compound trap. UI: removed the `disabled` attr + auto-uncheck-on-no-access wiring on the Docker (root) checkbox; updated help text; dropped the client-side guard. Tests: `test_root_without_access_invalid` flipped to `test_root_alone_valid` (4 cases on `TestDockerSelectionValidation`, still all pass; 168 total). (3) New doc `docs/jupyterhub-working-with-docker.md` - terse overview of the four user-visible modes + within-group combination table + across-group resolution + a mermaid two-socket diagram + the compound-group gotcha called out explicitly. Two-row addition to the combination tables in `limited-docker-access.md` and `docker-socket-permissions.md` for the new standalone-root mode. `pyproject.toml` 3.10.15 -> 3.10.16 from the operator rebuild, committed here. Files: `stellars_hub_services/docker_proxy.py`, `stellars_hub_services/groups_config.py`, `tests/test_group_resolver.py`, `html_templates_enhanced/groups.html`, `docs/jupyterhub-working-with-docker.md` (new), `docs/limited-docker-access.md`, `docs/docker-socket-permissions.md`, `pyproject.toml`.

163. **Task [Extended] - Central docker-proxy (register/unregister), kill per-user sidecars** (v3.10.17): Operator reaction to the per-user sidecar pattern - "wtf? we launch 2 docker containers per lab? NOOOO!" - plus live evidence that the sidecar disappeared between spawns (`docker ps` showed no `*-dockerproxy` despite the user being on `docker-limited`); architectural pivot from N sidecars to one central proxy with admin-API registration. Checkpoint `CHECKPOINT_BEFORE_CENTRAL_PROXY_3.10.17`<br>
    **Result**: Considered three layouts: proxy inside the lab (security trap - user can kill it or reach its `/var/run/docker.sock` mount), per-user sidecar (today, two containers per user, idempotency races), or shared central proxy with per-listener identity. Picked the third. New `stellars_docker_proxy.manager.Manager` holds `dict[user -> (AppRunner, UnixSite, ProxyConfig)]`; `register(user, overrides)` instantiates a fresh `ProxyConfig` + ProxyApp and binds a `UnixSite` at `<socket_dir>/<user>.sock`, replacing on re-register so quota edits take effect on next spawn. New `stellars_docker_proxy.admin.create_admin_app(manager, token)` exposes bearer-auth `GET/POST/DELETE /admin/registered/{user}` - the only privileged surface. Identity stays baked-at-socket on the data path - same model as the sidecar, just collapsed into one process. Rewrote `__main__` for env-driven central mode (`STELLARS_PROXY_*`); package bumped to 0.2.0. New `tests/test_manager.py` (8 cases) + `tests/test_admin.py` (9 cases) - 26 -> 43 proxy tests. Rewrote `stellars_hub_services.docker_proxy` as `aiohttp` admin-API client: `register_user`/`unregister_user`; `__init__.py` re-exports updated; `detect_self_image`/`ensure_user_proxy`/`stop_user_proxy` deleted (no docker-SDK dependency on the hub side anymore). `hooks.py` factory signature: `docker_proxy_image`/`docker_network_name` -> `docker_proxy_admin_url`/`_token`/`_socket_dir`; spawner bind-mounts the per-user socket file as `/run/dockersock/docker.sock`. `config/jupyterhub_config.py` reads the new env vars; `_post_stop_cleanup` calls `unregister_user`. `compose.yml` got a new `stellars-docker-proxy` service (same image as the hub via command override, host bind `/var/run/stellars-proxy:/var/run/stellars-proxy`, admin token required from `.env` via `${STELLARS_DOCKER_PROXY_ADMIN_TOKEN:?...}`). Hub gets `JUPYTERHUB_DOCKER_PROXY_ADMIN_URL=http://stellars-docker-proxy:9000` and the same token. `docs/jupyterhub-working-with-docker.md` + `docs/limited-docker-access.md` mermaid + module + env tables rewritten for the new model. Trade-offs flagged: stateless proxy means a crash drops all listeners (running limited users must restart their labs to re-register); process-compromise blast radius is "all limited users" (one process), acceptable for the convenience-driven threat model. 168 hub-services + 43 proxy = 211 tests pass; `python -m py_compile config/jupyterhub_config.py` clean; zero stale `ensure_user_proxy`/`stop_user_proxy`/`detect_self_image`/`JUPYTERHUB_DOCKER_PROXY_IMAGE` references in live code. `pyproject.toml` 3.10.16 -> 3.10.17 from the operator rebuild, committed here. Repo-only; needs image rebuild + `STELLARS_DOCKER_PROXY_ADMIN_TOKEN` in `.env`. Files: `stellars-docker-proxy/stellars_docker_proxy/manager.py` (new), `admin.py` (new), `__main__.py`, `__init__.py`, `tests/test_manager.py` (new), `tests/test_admin.py` (new), `stellars-hub-services/stellars_hub_services/docker_proxy.py`, `__init__.py`, `hooks.py`, `config/jupyterhub_config.py`, `compose.yml`, `docs/jupyterhub-working-with-docker.md`, `docs/limited-docker-access.md`, `pyproject.toml`.

164. **Task - Docker-proxy limits surfaced in the per-spawn [Groups] log line** (v3.10.18): Operator wanted both the docker-limited fact AND the imposed quotas/caps visible on the single per-user spawn log line, so triage stays one row per spawn instead of having to cross-reference the lower-level `registered docker-proxy for owner=...` audit line<br>
    **Result**: `hooks.py::pre_spawn_hook` now computes a `docker_limits` string when `resolved['docker_limited']` is True AND the registration wired `DOCKER_HOST` into `spawner.environment` (i.e. central proxy was reachable and `register_user` returned successfully), then formats it inline on the `[Groups]` info line as `docker_limits=[containers=N volumes=N networks=N storage_gb=N cpu=N mem_gb=N]`. The DOCKER_HOST guard intentionally distinguishes "limited resolved" from "limited resolved AND applied" - if the proxy was unreachable or the admin token missing, the line reads `docker_limited=True docker_limits=[-]` and the gap is obvious. Per-call audit line from `docker_proxy.py::register_user` is unchanged. Note: the spawn-time hook re-resolves group config + re-registers on every spawn, so admin edits to a group's quotas always take effect on the user's next lab start - no operator-side re-registration step needed. 168 hub-services tests still pass. `pyproject.toml` 3.10.17 -> 3.10.18 from the operator rebuild, committed here. 165. **Task [Extended] - Embed docker-proxy in-process; drop second container + admin HTTP + token** (v3.10.18): Operator reaction "why the fuck so complicated? cannot it be autogenerated and saved in data volume? we want this easy, enclosed in jupyterhub" after the central-proxy commit added a `stellars-docker-proxy` compose service + admin HTTP API + shared bearer token (`STELLARS_DOCKER_PROXY_ADMIN_TOKEN`) operators had to set in `.env`<br>
    **Result**: Reversed the central-mode design. The proxy now runs in-process inside the hub container - same asyncio loop the activity sampler and idle culler already run on. Zero new env vars to operators, zero admin HTTP, zero token, zero second container. Found a latent bug along the way: the central-mode `register_user` called `asyncio.run(...)` from inside the already-running async `pre_spawn_hook`, which would have raised `RuntimeError: cannot call asyncio.run() from a running event loop` the moment an operator actually wired the env vars. The in-process design avoids it entirely - everything's `await`ed on the right loop. Deletions: `stellars_docker_proxy/admin.py`, `__main__.py`, `tests/test_admin.py`. `stellars_docker_proxy` is now a pure library (`Manager`, `create_app`, `filters`, `quota`, `server`, `config`), bumped 0.2.0 -> 0.3.0. `stellars_hub_services/docker_proxy.py` rewritten: module-singleton `Manager` with lazy init (deferred to first call so the test env doesn't need the proxy on path), async `register_user`/`unregister_user` that `await mgr.register(...)` directly. `hooks.py` `make_pre_spawn_hook` factory signature: `docker_proxy_admin_url`/`_token`/`_socket_dir` -> just `docker_proxy_socket_dir` (default `/var/run/stellars-proxy`); the limited branch now `await register_user(...)`. `config/jupyterhub_config.py`: dropped admin URL/token reads; `_post_stop_cleanup` is async and awaits `unregister_user`. `compose.yml`: deleted the `stellars-docker-proxy` service block (~25 lines) + the 3 admin env vars from the hub; added one host bind `/var/run/stellars-proxy:/var/run/stellars-proxy` on the hub. `Dockerfile.jupyterhub`: new `ENV JUPYTERHUB_DOCKER_PROXY_SOCKET_DIR=/var/run/stellars-proxy` baked in (path is image-internal, not exposed to operators). Lifecycle is pure on-demand: hub boot creates no listener; the Manager is lazy-init'd on the first user pressing "Start My Server"; each spawn adds a `UnixSite` at `<socket_dir>/<user>.sock`, `post_stop_hook` tears it down. Hub restart wipes all listeners (stateless, same as the central design); the next spawn re-registers automatically. Checkpoint `CHECKPOINT_BEFORE_CENTRAL_PROXY_3.10.17` still covers this commit too (it brackets both directions of the experiment). Tests: 168 hub-services + 34 proxy = 202 passing (was 211; 9 admin tests gone with the deleted module). Docs `docs/jupyterhub-working-with-docker.md` + `docs/limited-docker-access.md` mermaid + module table + env table rewritten for the in-process model. Repo-only; needs image rebuild. No `.env` change. Files: `stellars_docker_proxy/__init__.py` (0.3.0), `admin.py` (deleted), `__main__.py` (deleted), `tests/test_admin.py` (deleted), `stellars-hub-services/stellars_hub_services/docker_proxy.py`, `hooks.py`, `config/jupyterhub_config.py`, `compose.yml`, `Dockerfile.jupyterhub`, `docs/jupyterhub-working-with-docker.md`, `docs/limited-docker-access.md`.

166. **Task [Extended] - Back per-user sockets with a named docker volume (no host path)** (v3.10.18): Operator pushback on the host bind: "I dont want to affect host, proxy happens entirely in the jupyterhub container, why the fuck access to /var/run/stellars-proxy ????". Live diagnostic confirmed the consequence - the live deployment uses the parent project's compose.yml which lacks the new host bind, so the hub wrote sockets into its own writable layer while Docker auto-created `/var/run/stellars-proxy/<user>.sock` as a stray directory on the host (failed bind-mount auto-create rule); the user's lab got that empty directory, hence "permission denied" on `docker ps`<br>
    **Result**: Replaced the host bind with a docker named volume `jupyterhub_docker` declared inline in `compose.yml`. The hub mounts it at `/var/run/stellars-proxy`; the spawner mounts the same volume into each user lab with Docker's `Subpath: <user>` option, exposing only the user's subdirectory containing a single `docker.sock`. Mount-level isolation preserved, no host filesystem manipulation, no `.env` change. Considered alternatives: TCP per-user port (no real boundary - any container on `jupyterhub_network` can reach any port and impersonate), TCP + mTLS client cert per user (CA + cert rotation + cert volume = too much for this scope), volume-subpath (chosen - Docker 25+ feature, mount-level boundary enforced by daemon). Confirmed `DOCKER_HOST=tcp://`... can't carry a path, so TCP routing-by-URL was a non-starter anyway. Code changes: `Manager` socket layout `<dir>/<user>.sock` -> `<dir>/<user>/docker.sock`; added `_clear_path` helper that handles stale files OR auto-created directories (covers the buggy state operators may already have on disk); unregister also `rmdir`s the empty user subdir. `stellars_hub_services.docker_proxy`: new `DEFAULT_VOLUME_NAME = 'jupyterhub_docker'`; path helper updated. `hooks.py::make_pre_spawn_hook` gains `docker_proxy_volume_name` param; limited branch now appends a `Mounts` entry to `spawner.extra_host_config` with `Type: volume`, `Source: jupyterhub_docker`, `Target: /run/dockersock`, `VolumeOptions.Subpath: <username>` - no more per-file bind. `config/jupyterhub_config.py` reads the new env var; `Dockerfile.jupyterhub` bakes `ENV JUPYTERHUB_DOCKER_PROXY_VOLUME=jupyterhub_docker` so it stays out of compose.yml. `compose.yml`: removed the host bind, added `jupyterhub_docker:` to the top-level `volumes:` block, hub volume mapping switched to `jupyterhub_docker:/var/run/stellars-proxy`. `stellars-docker-proxy` package version 0.3.0 -> 0.4.0 (socket path is a public-facing behavior change). New test `test_register_clears_stale_directory_at_socket_path` covers the leftover-directory recovery; 35 proxy + 168 hub-services = 203 tests passing. Docs (`docs/jupyterhub-working-with-docker.md`, `docs/limited-docker-access.md`) mermaid + lifecycle + env tables rewritten for the volume-backed model. Repo-only; needs image rebuild + `docker volume rm jupyterhub_docker` if operator wants to wipe state. Files: `stellars-docker-proxy/stellars_docker_proxy/manager.py`, `__init__.py` (0.4.0), `tests/test_manager.py`, `stellars-hub-services/stellars_hub_services/docker_proxy.py`, `hooks.py`, `config/jupyterhub_config.py`, `compose.yml`, `Dockerfile.jupyterhub`, `docs/jupyterhub-working-with-docker.md`, `docs/limited-docker-access.md`.

    **Result**: Word-boundary sed-renamed `/var/run/stellars-proxy` -> `/var/run/stellars-docker-proxy-sockets` across the 7 live files (compose.yml, Dockerfile.jupyterhub, jupyterhub_config.py, docker_proxy.py, hooks.py, limited-docker-access.md, jupyterhub-working-with-docker.md). So on first `make start` after image rebuild the README ends up inside `jupyterhub_docker` automatically; subsequent restarts preserve it. 168. **Task [Extended] - Docker-proxy volume namespace fix + fail outright on missing COMPOSE_PROJECT_NAME** (v3.10.18): Live spawn 404 on Subpath `<user>` of volume `jupyterhub_docker` - hub mounted compose-namespaced `${COMPOSE_PROJECT_NAME}_jupyterhub_docker` while `hooks.py` Mount Source used the bare `jupyterhub_docker`, so Docker silently auto-created an empty second volume and the Subpath lookup failed at `containers.start`<br>
    **Result**: Diagnosis: hub-side `docker inspect` showed `<project>_jupyterhub_docker -> /var/run/stellars-docker-proxy-sockets`; the daemon error path was `/var/lib/docker/volumes/jupyterhub_docker/_data/<user>` (no prefix). `Manager.register` was correctly creating the per-user subdir in the namespaced volume; the spawner's Mount API call was looking for that same subdir in the wrong volume. Followed the standard convention already established at `config/jupyterhub_config.py:178` for `f"{COMPOSE_PROJECT_NAME}_jupyterhub_shared"`: `JUPYTERHUB_DOCKER_PROXY_VOLUME` is now built in Python as `f"{COMPOSE_PROJECT_NAME}_jupyterhub_docker"` - no env-var read at all. Dropped `ENV JUPYTERHUB_DOCKER_PROXY_VOLUME=jupyterhub_docker` from `Dockerfile.jupyterhub`; the bare default in the image was exactly what allowed the mismatch to ship. Empty `COMPOSE_PROJECT_NAME` now raises `RuntimeError` at hub startup with a message citing the namespacing convention - the previous silent fallback `"jupyterhub"` was hiding the same class of bug. Removed the `try/except` wrapping `register_user` in the limited-docker branch of `pre_spawn_hook`: any setup failure (missing socket dir, empty volume name, `Manager.register` raising) now propagates and JupyterHub surfaces it as a failed spawn rather than silently downgrading the user to no-docker - operator explicitly asked for "fail outright". Added an upfront `RuntimeError` when either `docker_proxy_socket_dir` or `docker_proxy_volume_name` is empty, citing the username and the offending values. Volume README operator notes updated to show the namespaced on-disk name, the namespaced `docker volume rm` wipe command, and the `COMPOSE_PROJECT_NAME`-required behavior; doc/code references converted to GitHub URLs so the README is self-contained when read inside the volume. 168 stellars-hub-services tests still pass; proxy package untouched. Repo-only; needs image rebuild + lab restart. 170. **Task [Extended] - Docker-limited: 4 new group toggles + GroupConfigValidator + UI table redesign** (v3.10.18): Live trigger - a user's startup script `docker run -v <host-path>:/data` failed with the proxy's blanket "host path bind mounts are not allowed" reject, despite the user being in a `docker-root` (privileged lab) group. The hardcoded all-or-nothing `dangerous_reason()` had no caller-identity bypass, and the existing docker-limited config carried no toggles beyond quotas<br>
    **Result**: Four new per-group docker-limited toggles, all rendered in a redesigned `#docker-limited-options-table` (Bootstrap `Option`/`Enabled` columns - name + read-only description text per row, `.table-danger` styling on the danger row). (1) `docker_limited_allow_dangerous_flags` (default OFF) bypasses `dangerous_reason()` for host binds, host net/pid, cap-add, devices - independent of `docker_privileged`. (2) `docker_privileged` now also relaxes the `Privileged:True` rejection on user-spawned sub-containers (their lab is already kernel-root, so it grants nothing new). (3) `docker_limited_user_compose_project_enabled` (default ON) stamps ad-hoc `docker run` containers with a per-user `com.docker.compose.project` label rendered from new Dockerfile `ENV JUPYTERHUB_DOCKER_PROXY_USER_COMPOSE_PROJECT_TEMPLATE` (default `{compose_project}_{username}_containers`). (4) `docker_limited_user_compose_project_allow_override` (default ON) controls strict-mode rewriting of the user's `-p name`. (5) `docker_limited_reveal_hub_network` (default ON) special-cases `_list_networks_with_extras` to buffer-read upstream `/networks` and post-filter `is_owned(owner) OR Name in extras`, so users see the hub's docker network and can `--network <hub-net>` sidecars with DNS. `ProxyConfig` gains `allow_privileged` / `allow_dangerous_flags` / `allow_compose_project_override` / `extra_visible_networks`, wired from `_build_overrides` in hub-side `docker_proxy.py` (now takes `username`, `user_compose_project_template`, `hub_network_name` kwargs). New `GroupConfigValidator` class consolidates `validate_gpu`, `validate_docker` (+ limited-quota sanity), `validate_cpu` (new - positive cores when enabled), `validate_mem` (new - positive GB when enabled); PUT handler calls `validate_all` once with stable error codes (`invalid_gpu_selection` / `invalid_docker_selection` / `invalid_cpu_limit` / `invalid_mem_limit`); free `validate_gpu_selection` / `validate_docker_selection` kept as backward-compat wrappers. 176. **Task [Extended] - Proxy empty-body POST forwarding fix + button shrink/recentre** (v3.10.18): Live trigger - `01_onedrive_mount.sh` got past the host-bind reject (dangerous-flags toggle enabled) but `docker create` succeeded then `docker run` died with "starting container with non-empty request body was deprecated since API v1.22 and removed in v1.24". Worked when bypassing the proxy. Separately, operator on entry 175's flex-centred buttons: icons "still little too much to the left" - vertical centring fine, horizontal not<br>
    **Result**: Root cause in `server.py::_forward`: for any POST/PUT/PATCH without an explicit `body=` kwarg, the code did `data = request.content`, passing aiohttp's StreamReader to upstream. When the docker CLI sent NO body on `POST /containers/<id>/start` (modern API contract), aiohttp's client still upgraded the empty stream to `Transfer-Encoding: chunked` with a terminating `0\r\n\r\n` - dockerd treats that as a non-empty body and rejects on body-banned endpoints. Fix: gate the stream branch on `aiohttp.web.Request.body_exists` so empty-body POSTs forward as `data=None` (Content-Length: 0, no encoding upgrade). +1 regression test asserts the upstream call to `/containers/c1/start` carries no decodable body. Buttons separately reworked: dropped `fa-fw` (FA4's 1.28em bbox carried internal bearings that flex couldn't compensate for), pinned width to 2rem with zero horizontal padding so the flex content area equals button width, and shrank icons to `font-size: 0.85em` (operator: "tiny bit smaller"). Vertical kept natural (`btn-sm` padding + `align-items-center`). 63 proxy + 219 hub-services = 282 tests pass (was 281). Repo-only; needs image rebuild + lab restart. Files: `services/jupyterhub/stellars-docker-proxy/stellars_docker_proxy/server.py`, `services/jupyterhub/stellars-docker-proxy/tests/test_server.py`, `services/jupyterhub/html_templates_enhanced/groups.html`.

179. **Task [Extended] - Fix Stop Server flicker: poll spawner state instead of 1-second reload timer** (v3.10.18): User report: clicking Stop My Server caused screen flicker then Stop button reappeared - "user clicks on stop and nothing happens; screen flickers and the button stop server appears again". Stop genuinely worked server-side (DockerSpawner removed the container) but UI made it look broken<br>
    **Result**: Root cause in `home.html` MutationObserver: it watched JupyterHub's stock `home.js::$("#stop").click()` DOM flip (hide #stop, show #start), then triggered `setTimeout(location.reload, 1000)`. But on this deployment DockerSpawner stop takes ~60 sec (9P unmount + per-user docker.sock subpath unmount + workspace/cache/home volume unmounts), measured in entry 178's conversation as 61.5 sec. So the reload fired at t=1s, hub re-rendered Jinja using `default_server.active` which was still True (container still being torn down by Docker), template re-emitted the Stop button. Classic async-stop / sync-poll race. Replaced the observer + `setTimeout` with a polling loop: 1.5-second cadence on `GET /hub/api/users/<user>`, treating `server.ready === false && server.pending === null` (the exact definition JupyterHub uses server-side for `spawner.active`) as the "done" signal; 5-minute hard cap; network blips silently retry until cap. On poll success -> `location.reload()` exactly once (Jinja state guaranteed correct because the predicate matches). On cap timeout -> alert + dim the Start button with a tooltip directing user to refresh manually. Inline DOM updates as soon as stop click fires: Start button becomes "Stopping server..." with spinner, Stop button hidden, Restart hidden, session timer hidden - matches the eventual post-reload state so there's no flicker during the wait. Stock JupyterHub `home.js` handler still runs (we hook with `.on('click')`, not `.off`); both work in parallel without interfering. Repo-only; needs image rebuild + lab restart. 282 tests unaffected (UI-only change in template JS). Files: `services/jupyterhub/html_templates_enhanced/home.html`.

180. **Task [Extended] - Fix three stop-flow regressions: spinner overwrite + stale-state drift detector + Manage Volumes auto-reveal** (v3.10.18): Live-deploy retest of entry 179 surfaced three regressions: (1) clicking Stop showed no spinner animation; (2) /hub/home rendered "Stop My Server" button even after the server was fully stopped (DB row had `server_id=None`); (3) Manage Volumes button did not appear after stop<br>
    **Result**: Investigated live container: latest image deployed, poll code in place. Root causes diverge per symptom. (1) Stock JupyterHub `home.js::$("#stop").click()` success callback (fires ~50ms after click) runs `$("#start").text("Start My Server")` which ERASES the spinner DOM I had set on #start. Fix: stop fighting for `#start` content - hide BOTH `#stop` AND `#start` on click and inject a separate `#stop-spinner` element (`btn btn-lg btn-secondary disabled` with `fa-spinner fa-spin` + "Stopping server..." text). Stock home.js still mutates #stop and #start in its success callback but they are already hidden, so user sees no flicker. (2)+(3) Pre-existing class of bug: my polling logic only fired AFTER a user click - if the server got stopped via any other path (idle culler, admin stop, hub restart, CLI), the open page kept showing the stale "active" render forever. Added a **drift detector**: when Jinja renders the page with `default_server.active=True` (the `{% if %}` branch), a background `setInterval` polls `/hub/api/users/<user>` every 30 sec; on `isSpawnerInactive(userJson)` it auto-`location.reload()` - Jinja then re-renders with the inactive layout (Start button + Manage Volumes). Pauses while tab is hidden (`document.hidden`) so idle background tabs do not hammer the API; on `visibilitychange` to visible, fires one immediate check so stale tabs catch up fast. Pauses entirely during the stop click flow (the dedicated stop poll covers that window). The `{% else %}` branch (page rendered inactive) skips drift entirely - no wasted polls. Repo-only; needs image rebuild + lab restart. 282 tests unaffected. Files: `services/jupyterhub/html_templates_enhanced/home.html`.

181. **Task - Stop flow XSRF + reduced-motion spinner fixes** (v3.10.18): Entry 180's poll/drift logic landed but live testing exposed two new failures: page never reloaded after stop (stayed "Stopping..." indefinitely), and the spinner icon was static, not animating<br>
    **Result**: Hub log diagnosed the reload failure: `403 GET /hub/api/users/konrad.jelen?_=...: '_xsrf' argument missing from GET`. JupyterHub enforces XSRF on cookie-authenticated API calls including GETs - the AJAX poll never got a 200 so `isSpawnerInactive()` was never evaluated, the page hung on "Stopping...". Fix: both the stop-flow poll and the background drift detector now send `headers: { 'X-XSRFToken': getCookie('_xsrf') }`. Matches the existing restart-server POST handler pattern in the same file. Static spinner root cause: FontAwesome 7 (shipped in `/srv/venv/share/jupyterhub/static/components/@fortawesome/fontawesome-free/css/`) contains `@media (prefers-reduced-motion: reduce) { .fa-spin { animation: none !important } }` - any user with reduced-motion preference at the OS / browser level saw the FA spinner frozen. Switched the `#stop-spinner` injection from `<i class="fa fa-spinner fa-spin">` to Bootstrap's `<span class="spinner-border spinner-border-sm">`; Bootstrap's spinner only SLOWS the animation under prefers-reduced-motion rather than disabling it, so feedback is preserved as an accessibility-appropriate compromise. Repo-only; needs image rebuild + lab restart. Files: `services/jupyterhub/html_templates_enhanced/home.html`.

182. **Task [Extended] - Restart flow: poll until lab is responding instead of immediate reload** (v3.10.18): Operator request after stop flow stabilized in entry 181: "also server restart - we detect when server is online back when it starts responding from jupyterlab". The existing restart handler was symmetric to the pre-poll stop bug - it called `location.reload()` as soon as the POST `/api/users/<u>/restart-server` returned 200, but that endpoint only returns when Docker's `container.restart()` finishes; JupyterLab inside the container then needs further time to boot and respond. Reloading too early landed the user on a page that could not reach the lab (502s, redirects back to spawn-pending)<br>
    **Result**: Two-phase restart UX. Phase 1: modal button shows "Restarting container..." with Bootstrap `spinner-border` until the POST resolves. Phase 2: button switches to "Waiting for lab to come back online..." (same spinner, modal stays OPEN so the user sees the wait), and a new `pollUntilReady()` polls `/hub/api/users/<user>` every 1.5 sec watching for `isSpawnerReady(userJson)` - the mirror predicate of `isSpawnerInactive`: `server.ready === true && (server.pending === null || pending === undefined)`. Lab is considered ready ONLY when proxy route is established and `/user/<u>/` traffic flows. On ready -> `location.reload()`; on 5-min cap timeout -> modal closes, button re-enabled, alert directs user to refresh manually. Network blips (proxy 5xx during route re-establishment is common mid-restart) silently retried until cap. XSRF token sent on the GET (same fix as entry 181). The pre-existing "Server successfully restarted. Page will refresh." alert was misleading - fired before the lab was actually responding - removed. Repo-only; needs image rebuild + lab restart. Files: `services/jupyterhub/html_templates_enhanced/home.html`. Side note: operator flagged "took 62 seconds to stop" looks inflated since actual Docker remove < 10 sec; likely DockerSpawner `poll_interval` (default 30s) lag between Docker container removal and JupyterHub's confirmation poll - not addressed in this entry, candidate for separate investigation.

183. **Task [Extended] - TimingDockerSpawner: minimal-volume `[Timing]` probes for the lag investigation** (v3.10.20): Follow-up to entry 182's "62 sec stop" side note. Operator rejected a standalone diagnostic script ("slop") and asked for empirical timing measured INSIDE the actual stop/start/restart flows during real user actions, output to hub logs so it can be pulled later. Second pass after initial implementation: operator flagged the per-poll logging as too verbose ("too much per user, logs will grow dramatically") and asked for only critical info<br>
    **Result**: Created `stellars_hub_services/timing_spawner.py::TimingDockerSpawner`, a thin DockerSpawner subclass that wraps THREE lifecycle methods with ONE `[Timing]` log line each on method exit (no entry-side logging, no poll-loop spam): `start()` total spawn time, `stop()` total teardown as the hub observes it, `remove_object()` the actual Docker DELETE call (subset of stop). The delta `stop() elapsed - remove_object() elapsed` is the hub-side lag the operator flagged - small = Docker took the time (genuine teardown, e.g. 9P unmount), large = hub polling cadence or post-stop processing. Per user-action log volume: stop = 2 lines, start = 1 line, restart = 1 line (added via `[Timing]` wrap around `container.restart()` in `handlers/server.py::RestartServerHandler`). poll() NOT instrumented - it fires every 30s per active user and would flood the log. `config/jupyterhub_config.py` switched `spawner_class` from `dockerspawner.DockerSpawner` to the new subclass (single-line, easy to revert). Pull lines with `docker logs <hub> 2>&1 \\| grep '\\[Timing\\]'`. 219 hub-services tests still pass. `pyproject.toml` 3.10.18 -> 3.10.20 from operator rebuild, committed here. Files: `services/jupyterhub/stellars-hub-services/stellars_hub_services/{timing_spawner.py (new), handlers/server.py}`, `config/jupyterhub_config.py`, `pyproject.toml`.

184. **Task [Extended] - Restart UX: close modal, probe lab via CHP, plus silence proxy traceback on client disconnect** (v3.10.20): Operator report: live restart still went wrong. Three concerns. (1) The "Waiting for lab to come back online..." modal popup was unwanted: "I want for system to return to home view and temporarily disable the go to server button until we confirm that user's jupyterlab is back". Spawner ready bit fires when the proxy route is registered, NOT when JupyterLab actually accepts connections - that gap is where the bug lives. (3) Hub log spammed a full `ClientConnectionResetError` traceback from `stellars_docker_proxy.server._forward` on `POST /v1.54/containers/<id>/wait` whenever the docker CLI client (inside the lab) disconnected mid-stream during the restart<br>

Original HTML and href saved in closure for restoration. New `isLabResponding(callback)` does `GET {base_url}user/<u>/api?_=<ts>` through the public CHP proxy: statuses in {502, 503, 504, 0} mean CHP cannot reach the upstream lab (still booting), anything else (302 OAuth redirect, 401, 200) means the lab process is up and listening. `pollLabUntilResponding` retries every 1.5 sec up to 5 min; on responding -> restore `#start` from saved state, re-enable `#restart-server-btn`. On 5-min cap timeout -> alert, leave button disabled so operator notices. Restart button also disabled during the wait so user cannot double-trigger. On disconnect: log one DEBUG line, release upstream response, return cleanly.
