185. **Task [Extended] - Root-cause the 62s "slow to stop": aiohttp AppRunner shutdown_timeout default 60s blocks post_stop_hook** (v3.10.20): Operator: "konrad's server has already stopped - and the stopping server spinner still rolls; took nearly a minute". Entry 183's `TimingDockerSpawner` finally produced the empirical evidence: `[Timing] remove_object elapsed=0.009s` and `[Timing] stop elapsed=1.823s` - the Docker container was actually gone in under 2 sec. But hub still logged `User konrad.jelen server took 62.304 seconds to stop` 60 sec later, and the browser-side stop spinner kept rolling because `GET /hub/api/users/<u>` continued to report `server.ready=true` until that final clear. The gap had to be inside JupyterHub's `User.stop()` between `spawner.stop()` returning and the function exiting - i.e. somewhere in the finally block (`post_stop_hook`, `clear_state`, db commit, `auth.post_spawn_stop`)<br>
    **Result**: Traced to `_post_stop_cleanup` in `config/jupyterhub_config.py` -> `unregister_user` -> `Manager._stop()` -> `runner.cleanup()`. The aiohttp `AppRunner.cleanup()` call has `shutdown_timeout=60.0` as its inherited default from `BaseRunner.__init__` (verified live: `inspect.signature(web.BaseRunner.__init__)`). On stop, the lab container often has open long-poll requests to the per-user docker-proxy socket (most commonly `POST /v1.54/containers/<id>/wait` from the docker CLI). Those connections never drain cleanly because the lab is being torn down at the exact same moment, so `cleanup()` blocks until its full 60-sec timeout, which neatly explains the 62.3-sec total. Fix is one line in `stellars-docker-proxy/stellars_docker_proxy/manager.py::register()`: `runner = web.AppRunner(app, shutdown_timeout=5.0)`. Worst-case unregister latency now bounded to ~5 sec instead of 60. Chose 5 over 2 per operator ("5s is ok, 2 is too fine") - leaves headroom for genuine in-flight short requests to complete before the kill. Browser-side stop spinner was already correct; with the fix it should clear ~5 sec after the container is gone instead of after 60. 9/9 manager tests still green (no behaviour change in the happy path; only the worst-case shutdown wait shortens). Repo-only; needs image rebuild + lab restart. Files: `services/jupyterhub/stellars-docker-proxy/stellars_docker_proxy/manager.py`.

186. **Task [Extended] - Rewrite extra/docker_volume_backupper bash scripts in stdlib Python with curses picker, byte-percentage progress, multi-pattern matching** (v3.10.20): Operator: "the backup making script and simplify the options? it is a slop of a script; needs to be much simpler, also needs to have --dry-run option and by default it should require confirmation". Original `docker_volume_backupper.sh` took ONE positional regex, had no confirmation / no dry-run / no progress / no picker; `docker_volume_restore.sh` was equally bare. Subsequent operator clarifications shaped the final scope: multiple patterns OR-unioned, `--dry-run` + `-y/--yes` + `--no-progress` flags, curses-based interactive multi-select (rich rejected as third-party; curses is stdlib), per-volume byte-percentage progress bar, restore must match the same UX including streaming-progress and a sizes-included manifest in the picker<br>
    **Result**: Two new files under `extra/docker_volume_backupper/`, both stdlib-only (`argparse`/`subprocess`/`curses`/`threading`/`pathlib`; NO docker SDK, NO rich, NO whiptail). Old `.sh` pair deleted. `docker_volume_backupper.py`: positional args joined with `|` into a single `re` regex against `docker volume ls`, per-pattern "matched nothing" warnings, hard-fail only if total match set is empty. Pre-flight `du -sb` (60s timeout) inside an alpine container gives the uncompressed denominator; a daemon thread polls `out.stat().st_size` every 250 ms and renders `bytes_written / ~estimate (pct%)` via `\r\x1b[2K` redraw. Curses picker uses `curses.wrapper` for clean teardown, supports UP/DOWN/PgUp/PgDn/Home/End + SPACE + a/n/ENTER/q, parallel `list[bool]` selected state. Non-TTY guard exits 2 when stdin is piped and neither -y nor --dry-run given. `docker_volume_restore.py`: same shape, but progress mode splits into TWO docker runs - short wipe, then `docker run -i ... tar xzf - -C /data` with Python piping the tar.gz bytes into stdin via `subprocess.PIPE`. This makes numerator and denominator BOTH exact (bytes-sent vs file.stat().st_size); no pre-scan required. `--no-progress` keeps the original single combined `sh -c "rm ...; tar xzf /backup/..."` form via bind-mount, zero Python in the data path. Picker manifest shows per-file sizes and a running selection-bytes total in the footer; main listing also prints `(N files, total X GB)` and aligned `name | size | -> volume` columns. Verified live: 550 MB mikolaj cache → 527 MB tarball in 12.5s with smooth 0-99% bar; synthetic 200 MB random-data round trip (backup + corrupt + restore) confirmed bit-exact recovery in 5.0s + 2.6s. Non-TTY guard, pattern-no-match warning, missing-file/missing-volume skip, dry-run paths all exercised. neo4j-alienation could not be the demo target - inspect confirmed bind-mounts only, no named volumes; flagged to operator. Files: `extra/docker_volume_backupper/{docker_volume_backupper.py (new), docker_volume_restore.py (new)}`; deleted `docker_volume_backupper.sh` and `docker_volume_restore.sh`.

188. **Task [Extended] - docker_volume scripts: graceful Ctrl-C cleanup, modern UI (colours/bars/glyphs), inter-phase screen clear** (v3.10.20): Five-ask round on both backupper and restore scripts. (1) Ctrl-C must kill the docker container, remove the partial file, exit cleanly. (2) Apply everything to BOTH scripts. (3) Clear screen between picker close → confirm → progress phases. (4) Nicer/modern UI. (5) ANSI colours when supported. Also fielded the question of whether `tqdm` is stdlib - it is NOT, third-party `pip install tqdm`; declined to take the dep, kept the carriage-return approach. Also proposed but deferred: full curses dashboard showing overall + per-volume bars simultaneously (~200 LOC follow-up)<br>
    **Result**: Three subtle bugs surfaced while implementing Ctrl-C cleanup. (a) Bash sets SIGINT to `SIG_IGN` on background jobs and Python inherits + won't override; first `kill -INT` test was silently ignored. Fix: `signal.signal(signal.SIGINT, signal.default_int_handler)` at the top of `main()` so KI always fires regardless of how the script was launched. (b) `subprocess.run(cmd)` catches KI internally, calls `process.kill()` + `process.wait()` and the wait can block indefinitely on a graceful docker client teardown, so KI never re-raises into our except. Fix: switched both scripts to `subprocess.Popen + proc.wait()` so KI propagates immediately. (c) On Docker Desktop/WSL2 the host's bind-mount (e.g. `/tmp/voldemo`) is proxied to the docker VM via a 9P-style layer with deferred writes; after our `docker rm -f` returns and we `unlink()` the partial tarball, the daemon flushes pending writes ~500 ms later and re-creates the file, only settling ~2 sec later. Fix: `_try_remove_partial()` retry loop, up to 10 × 0.3-sec attempts, polling existence between each unlink so removal actually sticks. Cleanup path now: `docker rm -f` (daemon-side, since our killed client cannot reach the container any more) → `proc.kill/wait(timeout=5)` for the client → retry-unlink the partial. Modern UI lives in a tiny `_Style` class (`bold/dim/cyan/green/yellow/red/reset`) that no-ops when `not isatty()` or `NO_COLOR` is set or `TERM` is `dumb`. `fmt_bar(pct, width=24)` renders `[████░░░░░░] 67%` with U+2588/U+2591. Per-volume line goes from `▸ active` (cyan) to `✓ done` (green) to `✗ aborted/failed` (yellow/red). Listings use `•` bullets; restore manifest aligns name | size | -> volume columns. Run phase is framed with a 80-col `─...─` rule (also dimmed). `clear_screen()` (ANSI `\x1b[H\x1b[2J`, guarded on `isatty()`) fires after picker close and after final confirm so the user sees a clean run view. Curses picker also picks up colour via `start_color() + color_pair(1..3)` for title/help/checked-row; falls back to plain attrs if the terminal can't init colour pairs. Verified live: 800 MB synthetic-random backup completed cleanly in 18 s; Ctrl-C against a mid-flight backup produced `[1/1] ✗ ... aborted (container removed, partial file deleted)` + `Aborted by user.` + `rc=130` with NO orphan container and NO leftover partial after the WSL2 settle window. Discovered along the way that the test harness itself was eating SIGINT (bash inner-script dies on the same signal that goes to the process group), masking earlier "looks like cleanup didn't run" symptoms; `trap "" INT` in the test bash kept it alive to observe. Files: `extra/docker_volume_backupper/{docker_volume_backupper.py, docker_volume_restore.py}`.

189. **Task [Extended] - docker_volume scripts: kill duplicate banner line + add overall progress as a second refreshing line** (v3.10.20): Operator caught two issues in a real 5-volume run: each volume printed twice in the progress phase and there was no overall progress indicator. Duplicate cause: `backup_one`/`restore_one` opened with `prefix ...\n` and the poll thread then painted progress on the NEXT line via `\r\x1b[2K` - the banner was never overwritten, so the eventual `done` line landed on the progress line, leaving the orphan banner above<br>
    **Result**: Switched both scripts to a two-line refresh: when `show_progress` is on, we reserve two stacked lines upfront (per-item bar on line A, `Overall [bar] N%  (K/total done)` on line B) and park the cursor at line A with `\x1b[1A\r`. Each poll tick rewrites line A, `\n`s down, rewrites line B, then `\x1b[1A\r`s back. On exit (success / failure / KI cleanup) we clear both lines and park the cursor at line A so the final done / aborted print overwrites the banner and leaves the cursor below line B - no orphan, no duplicate. Overall fraction is computed locally as `((idx - 1) + min(1, current_bytes / current_estimate)) / total` so no pre-flight `du` of every selected item is needed; each item counts as one equal-weight slot. `--no-progress` path unchanged (single banner + done line). Verified on a 2-volume backup (50 MB + 30 MB) round-tripped through restore: overall bar climbed 0 → 50 → 99 % across the two items, `(0/2 → 1/2)` counter advanced cleanly, no duplicates. Files: `extra/docker_volume_backupper/{docker_volume_backupper.py, docker_volume_restore.py}`.

193. **Task [Extended] - Hub-side lab-ready probe to silence devtools 503s during restart poll** (v3.10.20): Operator pasted browser devtools showing `GET .../user/<u>/api ... 503 (Service Unavailable)` repeating for every tick of the post-restart poll loop (`home.html` `isLabResponding` / `pollLabUntilResponding`). "no need to have errors, it can be captured and handled and still inform ui when server is back". Root behaviour: browsers log every failed network request (≥ 400 / connect errors) to devtools regardless of how JS handles the response - there is no JS API to suppress that. The only fix is to not make a request that returns 5xx<br>
    **Result**: New hub-side endpoint `GET /hub/api/users/{username}/lab-ready` that always returns HTTP 200 with `{"ready": bool, "status"|"reason": ...}`, doing the actual lab probe server-side. Handler `services/jupyterhub/stellars-hub-services/stellars_hub_services/handlers/lab_ready.py::LabReadyHandler`: auth checks (current user or admin), 200 with `ready:false reason:not_active` if spawner is inactive or `server` attribute missing, otherwise issues an async `tornado.httpclient.AsyncHTTPClient.fetch(GET, connect_timeout=2, request_timeout=5, follow_redirects=False, raise_error=False)` against the upstream lab URL built from `spawner.server.{proto,ip,port,base_url}` (bypassing CHP so a not-yet-listening lab gives a fast ConnectionRefused instead of the longer CHP-503 path). Connect errors / timeouts caught, returned as `ready:false reason:<ExceptionClass>`; any HTTP response (200, 302, 401, even 5xx from the lab itself) means the lab process is up and serving - mirrors the client-side `blockedStatuses = [502, 503, 504, 0]` heuristic exactly, just server-side. Registered in `handlers/__init__.py` (export + `__all__` count 21 -> 22) and `config/jupyterhub_config.py` (import alphabetised between `HealthCheckHandler` and `ManageVolumesHandler`, route `r'/api/users/([^/]+)/lab-ready'` added next to the existing restart-server route). `home.html::isLabResponding` rewritten to call the new endpoint with `X-XSRFToken` header, reading `data.ready` from the JSON response; on AJAX error (network blip / auth issue) returns false so the poll loop simply retries. 219 hub-services tests pass (had to bump the handler-count assertion in `test_imports.py` 21 -> 22). Repo-only; needs image rebuild + lab restart. Files: `services/jupyterhub/stellars-hub-services/stellars_hub_services/handlers/{lab_ready.py (new), __init__.py}`, `services/jupyterhub/stellars-hub-services/tests/test_imports.py`, `services/jupyterhub/html_templates_enhanced/home.html`, `config/jupyterhub_config.py`.

For spawn-pending: the EventSource at `/api/users/<u>/server/progress` hangs because JupyterHub's `SpawnProgressAPIHandler` 400s when `_spawn_pending` is False (we restarted the container via Docker, never called `spawner.start()`), yielding no `ready`/`failed` event so the page sits forever. 196. **Task [Extended] - Fix flapping per-user favicon CHP route (stock favicon leak) + no-flap tests** (v3.10.20): Operator: konrad.jelen's JupyterLab tab shows the stock favicon, not the custom Stellars one. Investigation proved the whole server-side chain is correct - custom favicon (`md5 aeda2792…`) copied to hub static, served `200` at `/hub/static/favicon.ico`; lab template references `{{ base_url }}static/favicons/favicon.ico` (the overridden path); a direct `curl` of the proxied favicon returns `302 -> /hub/static/favicon.ico`. Yet the hub log showed the per-user favicon route being deleted then re-added every 5-minute `check_routes()` cycle - the route flaps, and during the deleted windows the request falls through CHP's generic `/user/<u>/` route to the lab, which serves its own stock icon, and the browser caches it<br>
    **Result**: Root cause is a trailing-slash mismatch. `ConfigurableHTTPProxy.get_all_routes()` -> `_routespec_from_chp_path()` (`jupyterhub/proxy.py:901-915`) ALWAYS appends a trailing slash, so `check_routes()` sees the live route as `/user/<u>/static/favicons/favicon.ico/`, but `pre_spawn_hook`/`schedule_startup_favicon_callback` stored the `extra_routes` key WITHOUT the slash. The `if routespec not in good_routes` test (built from extra_routes keys verbatim) therefore flags the route stale on every cycle and queues a `delete_route()` in the SAME `asyncio.gather()` as the re-add - both resolve to the same CHP path, a race, so the route is nondeterministically present/absent. Verified empirically with the real proxy: raw key `!=` round-trip (flaps), `validate_routespec(key) ==` round-trip (stable). Fix: one line at each of the two favicon registration loops in `stellars_hub_services/hooks.py` - `routespec = app.proxy.validate_routespec(routespec)` before `add_route` + `extra_routes` assignment, normalizing to JupyterHub's own canonical trailing-slash form so the keys match and the route is never stale. `add_route` strips the slash again via `_routespec_to_chp_path` for the actual CHP POST, and CHP path matching is slash-insensitive (segment trie), so storage, matching, and the `FaviconRedirectHandler` 302 are all unchanged - only the bookkeeping key changes. Kept the existing architecture (per-user CHP override -> hub redirect -> hub static) rather than baking the favicon into the separate lab image, since the override lets the operator rebrand at the hub without touching `stellars-jupyterlab-ds`. Added 8 regression tests to `tests/test_favicon.py` using the real `ConfigurableHTTPProxy` helpers and a faithful slice of the `check_routes()` stale-detection logic: canonical key matches the CHP round-trip and survives check_routes with zero stale deletions; the old slash-less key does NOT match (a guard that fires if upstream slash handling ever changes) and gets deleted every cycle; `validate_routespec` is idempotent; and `TestHookWritesCanonicalRoutes` drives the actual `pre_spawn_hook` (mocked hub/proxy) to assert the keys it writes are canonical, that `add_route` and `extra_routes` agree, and that those real keys survive simulated check_routes - covering both the `favicon.ico` and `favicon-busy` routes. Full suite 227 passed (was 219). Repo-only; needs image rebuild + hub restart to land, and affected browsers hard-refresh once to evict the cached stock icon. Files: `services/jupyterhub/stellars-hub-services/stellars_hub_services/hooks.py`, `services/jupyterhub/stellars-hub-services/tests/test_favicon.py`.

198. **Task [Extended] - Redesign session-extension on a ceiling-bounded deadline (fix banking, idle-countdown, max-extend, progress bar)** (v3.10.22): Operator found konrad's server showing TTL 72h (max), an "idle" badge, and a 60% bar at once. Live DB + jupyter-server source investigation showed a structural flaw, not a display bug: the extension model was an UNCAPPED growing budget (`effective = base + extension_hours_used*3600`), and each extend added to `extension_hours_used` while the idle clock (`now - last_activity`) kept running, so repeated "idle then refill" cycles banked past the ceiling - konrad reached `extension_hours_used=90h` -> `effective=114h` vs a 72h ceiling. `remaining = clamp(effective - elapsed, 0, ceiling)` clamped only the DISPLAY to 72h while the culler enforced the 114h budget, so the server would actually live ~114h idle and the bar read `clamped_remaining/unclamped_effective = 72/114 = 63%`. Separately confirmed the "active" signal is HTTP `api_last_activity` (jupyter_server `base/handlers.py:805`) from frontend polling (jupyter-resource-usage `/api/metrics/v1` ~2s, kernels/sessions/terminals/workspaces), NOT kernel activity (no kernels running) - reported to the hub by `jupyterhub.singleuser.mixins.notify_activity`; that root cause is lab-side and left for `stellars-jupyterlab-ds`<br>
    **Result**: Replaced the budget model with a ceiling-bounded cull deadline stored in `spawner.state['cull_at']`. `remaining = clamp(max(cull_at - now, base - (now - reference)), 0, ceiling)` where `reference = last_activity or started`: the deadline term bounds lifetime at the ceiling (no banking - ever), the `base - idle` activity floor keeps an active server at >= base, and extend pushes the deadline out (capped at `now + ceiling`) so replenish refills up to but never past the ceiling and "max means max" is structural (no sub-hour shortfall). Rewrote `idle_culler.py` pure layer to seconds-in/seconds-out functions (`calc_remaining`, `calc_available_hours(remaining, ceiling)`, `calc_extended_remaining`, `should_cull(remaining, age, max_age)`, kept `calc_ceiling`) plus a `remaining_seconds_for(orm_spawner, base, ceiling, now)` runtime helper that is the single source for the three callers and migrates legacy `extension_hours_used` derive-on-read (`reference + min(base + ext*3600, ceiling)`) with no bulk pass - the first extend persists `cull_at` and drops the legacy key. `run_cull_pass`/`schedule_idle_culler` now take `ceiling_seconds` (wired from `config/jupyterhub_config.py` as base + max_extension*3600). `handlers/session.py` (both handlers) and `handlers/activity.py` dashboard now compute remaining via the helper; session-info drops `extensions_used_hours`. `session-timer.js` bar denominator switched from `effective` to the ceiling (`timeout + max_extension_hours*3600`) so the ceiling reads exactly 100% and a fresh server reads base/ceiling=33% (intentional, visualises extension headroom); removed all `extensions_used_hours` usage in `updateUI`/`startCountdown` and the two extend callbacks. Dead code removed: `calc_effective_timeout`, `calc_time_remaining`, `calc_new_extensions`, `calc_extension_for_max` and their `__init__` exports. Rewrote `tests/test_idle_culler.py` as parametrized scenario matrices: `calc_remaining` (deadline vs activity-floor vs clamp), the floored replenish offer, `calc_extended_remaining` + a hard-cap regression sweep, `should_cull`, a 15-row lifecycle matrix through `remaining_seconds_for` (fresh/active/idle/legacy/deadline/garbage-fallback), and integration tests including konrad's exact case (90h legacy, idle 13h -> 59h, then max-extend -> exactly 72h) and "repeated idle->extend cycles never exceed the ceiling". 51 idle-culler tests pass, full suite 235 passed; Python + JS compile clean. Repo-only; needs image rebuild + hub restart to land - after which konrad's TTL reads ~59h and counts down, the bar ~82%, and the server is culled at 72h idle not 114h. Files: `services/jupyterhub/stellars-hub-services/stellars_hub_services/{idle_culler.py, __init__.py, handlers/session.py, handlers/activity.py}`, `services/jupyterhub/stellars-hub-services/tests/test_idle_culler.py`, `services/jupyterhub/html_templates_enhanced/static/session-timer.js`, `config/jupyterhub_config.py`.

199. **Task [Extended] - API keys pool group config (acceptance criteria + library implementation)** (v3.11.0): Operator requested a new group-config type (alongside env vars, GPU, Docker, compute, memory): a pool of API credentials handed to user containers so no two RUNNING containers share a key, with credentials returned on stop, resilient reconciliation from running containers (not stop events, since a container may stop while the hub is down or run a prior hub version), empty vars + warning on exhaustion, and last-4-only logging. Worked in planning mode: wrote `docs/acc-crit-api-keys-pool.md` (31 acceptance criteria AC-1..AC-31) as the contract, then a Plan-agent-validated implementation plan, then built it<br>
    **Result**: New self-contained library module `stellars_hub_services/api_keys_pool.py` mirroring `idle_culler.py`/`docker_proxy.py`: a stdlib-only pure layer (`mask_last4`, `normalize_pool`, `pick_free_slot`, `env_for_slot`, `assignment_mask_str`, `merge_pool_on_save`, `mask_pool_in_config`, `pool_label_key`/`parse_pool_labels`), a runtime observer (`observe_in_use` reads running `jupyterlab-*` container labels off the main loop via the `docker_utils` executor), a threading-singleton `PoolManager` whose `assign` closes the create-window race with an `asyncio.Lock` + tentative reservations and reuses a user's existing slot on duplicate spawn, plus `reconcile` and startup/periodic schedulers. Durable marker is a Docker label `tech.stellars.apikeys.pool.<group>.slot=<slot>` carrying the stable slot id only - never the secret - so the in-use set is always re-derived from reality and legacy/unlabelled containers hold no slot. `groups_config.py` gained the nested `api_keys_pool` default (mode pair/single, env var names, credentials with stable `slot` ids) and `validate_api_keys_pool` (mode required, var names per mode, no half-credentials) registered in `_ALL`. `group_resolver.py` collects pools as a priority-ordered LIST (not scalar-merged) and now also records `env_var_source` (group index per plain env var) so a pool-var vs plain-env-var clash resolves by group order, honouring the operator's "higher group in the ordered list wins" rule across BOTH kinds, not just pool-vs-pool. `hooks.py` `pre_spawn_hook` calls `PoolManager.assign`, applies env with the group-order tiebreak (logging shadows), merges durable labels into `extra_create_kwargs['labels']`, and logs each assignment masked / exhaustion as a warning. `handlers/groups.py` PUT does the mask round-trip merge (`merge_pool_on_save` keeps a stored secret when the incoming value is the masked sentinel for a known slot, mints slot ids for new entries) + reserved-name rejection, and all three response paths mask secrets via `mask_pool_in_config`. `config/jupyterhub_config.py` wires `schedule_startup_api_keys_reconcile` + `schedule_api_keys_reconcile` (reusing the cull cadence) and a best-effort `PoolManager.release_tentative` in `_post_stop_cleanup`. `__init__.py` re-exports the public surface. Added `tests/test_api_keys_pool.py` (pure-layer matrices, mask round-trip, PoolManager exclusivity/reuse/exhaustion/multi-pool/group-order, reconcile reap+promote) plus pool cases in `test_validator.py` and `test_group_resolver.py`: full suite 295 passed, package + config compile clean. `pyproject.toml` 3.10.23 -> 3.11.0. Backend/library complete; the admin UI form in `groups.html` and end-to-end verification are the remaining follow-up, and the feature needs an image rebuild + hub restart to land. Files: `docs/acc-crit-api-keys-pool.md`, `services/jupyterhub/stellars-hub-services/stellars_hub_services/{api_keys_pool.py, groups_config.py, group_resolver.py, hooks.py, handlers/groups.py, __init__.py}`, `services/jupyterhub/stellars-hub-services/tests/{test_api_keys_pool.py, test_validator.py, test_group_resolver.py}`, `config/jupyterhub_config.py`, `pyproject.toml`.

205. **Task - Abuse / DDoS protection (Traefik rateLimit + hub limits)** (v3.11.2): Operator asked how to protect the hub and labs (both behind the proxy) from DDoS; planned in plan mode, then implemented env-driven L7 abuse protection with the logic baked into the library so `jupyterhub_config.py` stays thin wiring<br>

Layer B: new pure-stdlib `stellars_hub_services/abuse_protection.py` with garbage-tolerant `parse_int`, `build_app_protection`, `ratelimit_disabled`, and `apply_abuse_protection(c, env)` wiring `concurrent_spawn_limit` (100), `active_server_limit` (0), NativeAuth lockout (5 attempts / 600s; `0` = no-op) - config is one call. 210. **Task [Extended] - Implement group-gated file downloads** (v3.11.5): Built the best-effort hub-side download blocker specced in entry 209, after live probing reshaped the design<br>
    **Result**: Probed the running lab as `konrad.jelen` and found the design assumptions wrong in two ways that changed the approach. (1) The container user `lab` has passwordless sudo and open egress (github/pypi reachable, curl/scp/ssh present), so no HTTP control is a security boundary - reframed with the operator as best-effort policy + notification + audit, not exfiltration prevention. (2) "Path filtering not enough": jupyter_server sets `Content-Disposition: attachment` on `files/`/`nbconvert/` only when `?download` is truthy (verified in source), and there are extra vectors beyond `/files/` - `jupyterlab_export_markdown_extension` `export/{docx,pdf,html}` (POST, always attachment) and `jupyterlab_share_files_extension` `public/share/.../download` (unauthenticated public link). Dropped the planned `Sec-Fetch-Dest` logic for the download-arg/Content-Disposition discriminator. Implementation: `downloads_active` grant in `groups_config.py` + `group_resolver.py` (`downloads_allowed`, OR across groups) + `handlers/groups.py` accept; new `handlers/downloads.py` with `DownloadBlockHandler` (pure-download prefixes, 403 no-auth) and `FilesGuardHandler` (auth, owner-or-admin, block on download-arg else reverse-proxy to the container forwarding Range, defense-in-depth attachment block) plus a throttled `notify_blocked` (10s/user aggregate, reuses notifications-extension ingest); `hooks.py` registers/removes per-user CHP block routes (favicon-route pattern, `extra_routes` survival) gated on `block_file_downloads`, with `schedule_startup_downloads_callback` for restart survivors; `config/jupyterhub_config.py` reads `JUPYTERHUB_BLOCK_FILE_DOWNLOADS` (default 0, dormant) and wires factory + startup callback + log; `settings_dictionary.yml` entry; `groups.html` File Downloads section + Downloads badge. Lab core (contents API, kernels, terminals, static, inline viewers) untouched. Tests: `TestDownloadsAllowed` + `TestIsDownloadArg`/`TestFilenameFromPath`; 385 passed (+11). README + acc-crit doc rewritten to the implemented design. Live end-to-end pending an operator hub rebuild/restart.

212. **Task - Rework file downloads to section-gated priority-wins** (v3.11.5): Operator wanted per-group downloads configured explicitly with the higher-priority group winning - the grant-only OR shipped in entry 210 could only ever exempt a member, never explicitly block one, and an off section was still read as "not granted" rather than "not configured"<br>
    **Result**: Converted the File Downloads control to the same model as sudo (entry 211): section-gated, priority-wins, platform default as fallback. `groups_config.py` adds `downloads_allow` (True) beside the now-section-gate `downloads_active`; `group_resolver.py` returns `downloads_allow` tri-state (first configuring group's value walking priority-descending, else `None`) instead of the boolean `downloads_allowed`; `handlers/groups.py` accepts the new key. `hooks.py` enforcement now gates on `block_file_downloads or downloads_allow is not None` and computes block as `not downloads_allow` when configured else the `JUPYTERHUB_BLOCK_FILE_DOWNLOADS` default - so a high-priority group can block even when the platform default is allow, or allow even when it is block; the startup-survivor callback follows the same rule and stays dormant only when default-allow and no group configures. `groups.html` gains an inner allow/block toggle and a `Downloads on/off` badge; `settings_dictionary.yml`, the acc-crit doc and the README (terse technical-doc rewrite) reworded from grant-exemption to default-fallback. `TestDownloadsAllowed` rewritten as `TestDownloadsAllow` (tri-state priority-wins); 394 passed. Hub-side only; live pending operator restart.

213. **Task - Fix download-block redirect loop + terse group section text** (v3.11.5): Operator hit `ERR_TOO_MANY_REDIRECTS` opening a file as a downloads-blocked user (`konrad.jelen`); also asked to trim the verbose group-config section descriptions<br>
    **Result**: Root cause - `FilesGuardHandler` was a JupyterHub `BaseHandler` with `@web.authenticated`, but it is mounted at `/user/{u}/...` where the hub login cookie (path `/hub/`) is never sent, so `get_current_user()` returned None and 302'd to `/hub/login`, which (authenticated there) bounced back to the file, looping forever - the guard body never ran so no block/notify fired. Converted `FilesGuardHandler` in `handlers/downloads.py` to a plain `tornado.web.RequestHandler`: dropped `@web.authenticated` and the hub owner-or-admin check, replaced `self.find_user`/`self.log` with `JupyterHub.instance()`; isolation holds because the reverse-proxy forwards the `/user/{u}/` cookie to the container, which the browser only sends to that user's own prefix. Separately swept all `groups.html` section descriptions (env vars, GPU, memory, CPU, volume mounts, API keys, downloads, sudo, docker quota fields) to terse effect+priority+why, dropping env var names and injection mechanics; fixed the Volume Mounts header icon (`fa-hdd-o`, a FA4 name absent from the solid set, rendered blank) to `fa-hard-drive`. `py_compile` clean; needs restart.

214. **Task - Block JupyterLab download button via Sec-Fetch-Dest** (v3.11.6): Live test as `konrad.jelen` (downloads-blocked group) showed README.md still downloading - the `?download` arg discriminator missed JupyterLab's Download command, which saves client-side via `<a download>` against `files/<path>` with NO arg, so jupyter_server served it 200 inline and the browser wrote it to disk<br>
    **Result**: Reworked `FilesGuardHandler` (`handlers/downloads.py`) to classify by the browser's `Sec-Fetch-Dest` header instead of the query arg alone. New `_is_download_request`: blocks a truthy `?download`, and (GET/HEAD only) blocks `Sec-Fetch-Dest` of `empty` (fetch / `<a download>`), `document` (open-in-tab), or absent (fail-closed); allows inline-media dests (`image`/`video`/`audio`/`font`/`style`/`object`/`embed`/`iframe`/...). POST left on the arg check so nbconvert inline conversion is not caught. Per-vector dests captured empirically via Playwright over Traefik HTTPS (synthetic `<a download>` reports `empty`, `<img>` reports `image`). Live-verified against the genuine download event (`expect_download` -> `Download.path: canceled`, bytes never saved): button/`?download=1`/open-tab all 403 with matching `via=sec-fetch-dest=empty|download-arg|sec-fetch-dest=document` audit lines, inline image 200, notify ingest POST 200. `TestIsDownloadRequest` added; 403 tests pass (build-gated by the Dockerfile pytest step). acc-crit doc updated. Hub-side only; bake on rebuild.

216. **Task [Extended] - Unify group permissions into a policy-type registry** (v3.12.0): Group permissions were defined three-plus times over - `default_config()`'s flat field bag, `resolve_group_config()`'s per-feature merge `if`s, `GroupConfigValidator` + the `GroupsConfigHandler.put` if-chain, and the UI - so every new permission meant editing all of them in lockstep and the combine rules (OR-grant, biggest-wins, priority-wins, list-union) lived as scattered, un-inspectable branches; operator asked for one model where each group resolves to a policy and policies resolve across groups into a user-policy object, with per-type drivers for the complex cases<br>
    **Result**: New `stellars_hub_services/policy/` package - `registry.py` holds one `PolicyType` per permission (env_vars, gpu, docker, mem, cpu, sudo, downloads, api_keys, volume_mounts) declaring `default`, `coerce` (set-rule, may raise `PolicyCoerceError`), `validate`, `resolve` (owns its combine strategy + internal supersede e.g. raw-docker-beats-limited), an optional `DriverRef` (api_keys -> `PoolManager`, docker -> proxy `register_user`), and `ui.summarize`; `engine.py` exposes `resolve_policies` (drop-in for the deleted `resolve_group_config`, same signature + output key set), `default_config`, `validate_all`, `coerce_config`. `groups_config.py` now delegates default/validation and re-exports mountpoint constants; `handlers/groups.py` PUT collapsed to a registry coerce+validate loop; `hooks.py` three call sites repointed. Chose full migration with no shim per operator directive - to license deleting `resolve_group_config` and `GroupConfigValidator` outright, first froze the legacy resolver output across a 38-scenario matrix (`tests/_policy_scenarios.py` -> `tests/golden/policy_resolution.json`) via a one-off generator, then proved `resolve_policies` reproduces it deep-equal (`test_policy_golden.py`); only then deleted `group_resolver.py` and the validator. api-keys hub-restart persistence (a lab outlives the hub; in-memory release tracking would collide) confirmed label-derived and tested in `TestRestartPersistence` - survivors keep their slot, a third spawn never re-hands a live slot, exhaustion over collision. Added `test_policy_coerce.py` (set-rules) and `test_policy_bundle.py` (export/import round-trip of the `{group_name, description, priority, policies}` bundle - foundation for import/export). `groups.html`: group name opens config (cog dropped) with a hover tooltip listing active policies from a JS mirror of `ui.summarize`. 471 tests pass (+68). Tracked in `docs/acc-crit-group-policy-model.md`. Hub-side only; needs rebuild.

219. **Task [Extended] - Policy models own apply + restart lifecycle (controller layer)** (v3.12.0): The resolution side was clean (a registry) but application was the opposite - `hooks.py::pre_spawn_hook` was a ~340-line monolith with a hardcoded branch per feature plus three separate startup callbacks, so "clean resolve, frankenstack apply"; operator wanted each policy type to be a self-contained model that both resolves AND imposes itself, with a controller for making each policy work<br>
    **Result**: Converted the function-based registry into model classes. Regression guard: new `tests/test_policy_apply.py` drives a `FakeSpawner` (and fake app/proxy + monkeypatched `register_user`/`observe_in_use`) asserting exact spawner state per model - gpu all/specific/none, mem+swap, cpu ceil, sudo on/off/default, env, volume add+unmount-on-leave, docker raw/none/privileged/limited, downloads block/allow/dormant, api-keys assign + label + env-precedence. The resolve golden and every prior suite stay green; 506 tests pass (+31). Pure structural move - no apply behaviour changed; `docs/acc-crit-group-policy-model.md` controller section reworked. Needs rebuild.

221. **Task [Extended] - Local functional test harness + unit-test CI split** (v3.12.2): Split tests into fast pytest suites (now a GitHub `unit_tests` job, previously only run inside the image build) and a new local-only functional regression harness that boots the real image and drives the running platform end-to-end - GitHub runners cannot run the DockerSpawner container deployment, so it stays local<br>
    **Result**: New `tests/functional/` package: `compose.functional.yml` boots a fully isolated throwaway deployment (own compose project `stellars-functest`, own network, project-namespaced volumes, dedicated `functestadmin`, no published host port) plus a containerized Playwright runner (`mcr.microsoft.com/playwright/python`) joined to the test network and given the docker socket so tests can `inspect`/`exec` spawned labs. `make test-functional` boots -> runs everything -> cleans up (containers/network/volumes; pulled images kept to avoid re-pull, `REMOVE_IMAGES=1` to drop them) and prints total time; `PYTEST_ARGS="-k ..."` allows selective re-runs but the default runs all. Teardown is scoped strictly to `stellars-functest`/`functestadmin` so the operator's real deployment is never touched (verified zero leftover resources). Key debugging: admin login failed because env-password bootstrap (`_provision_admin_userinfo`) cannot seed on a single fresh boot - the `users_info` table is created after the config runs - so the harness uses the bootstrap-by-signup window (a `conftest` fixture signs up the first admin, then authenticates); cross-test pollution + a lagging in-place table re-render were fixed with an API-based `clean_groups` autouse fixture (wipes groups before/after each test) and a reload-after-delete assertion. Tests: bootstrap, login/branding, group/policy lifecycle (create -> name-opens-config -> toggle -> save -> persist -> delete), multi-policy badges+tooltip, priority reorder, settings/activity/notifications, health, best-effort spawn smoke (minimal `quay.io/jupyterhub/singleuser`), and a conditional GPU auto-detection test that reads the hub `[GPU debug]` startup line (skips on CPU-only hosts; `FUNCTEST_GPU_ENABLED=2` on a GPU host). 10 passed, 1 skipped in ~89s. `docs/acc-crit-functional-test-harness.md` is a ~200-criterion catalogue including the group-config -> running-container effect matrix (per-policy `docker inspect` assertions) and hub+lab-container branding - the planned backlog the harness grows into. The image build (`make build`) gates on the unit suites and produced 3.12.2.

222. **Task [Extended] - Functional harness: container-policy + env-auth + GPU; drop always-skip tests** (v3.12.2): Built the two open functional-harness items (group-config -> running-container inspection, and the signup-disabled env-password auth mode) and reconfigured the suite so every test actually executes - the operator's principle that a test which always skips is noise<br>
    **Result**: `test_container_policy.py` is the core end-to-end check - it configures a group (sudo-off, env `FOO=bar`, 2GB mem, a volume mount) via the admin API, adds `functestadmin`, spawns the server, and `docker inspect`s the real `jupyterlab-functestadmin` container, asserting `JUPYTERLAB_SUDO_ENABLE=0`, the env var, `HostConfig.Memory`, the volume mount and the compose label. A `conftest` `pytest_collection_modifyitems` hook deselects (never skips) tests outside the run's regime - envauth only in env mode, gpu only when GPU is on. Result: default `make test-functional` runs 12 tests, 0 skipped, ~26s; env mode runs 2 tests in 1.5s. 224. **Task [Extended] - Portal rebuild insights + concept**: Operator wanted the sweep's analysis and a target architecture for a future complete frontend rebuild written into the catalogue, framed by the hard requirement that hub and lab are two different systems with the hub as gateway/proxy/authenticator guarding everything<br>
    **Result**: Extended `docs/portal-ui-catalogue.md` with two analysis sections. `## Rebuild insights` records the cross-cutting findings: three rendering paradigms stitched together (Jinja + a stock React admin SPA + vanilla JS), the worst seam being the admin page where the custom layer intercepts React's own `fetch()` and injects DOM via a MutationObserver; the policy registry as the one subsystem built right (server computes `policy_summary`, client renders verbatim) and the pattern the rest should follow; state management being full-page reload (the lagging-table bug from the functional harness was a direct symptom); polling sprawl (six independent loops, only spawn progress uses a real stream); mobile as a fork not a responsive layout (`mobile.js` reimplements start/stop/status/activity); two pockets of framework-born complexity (first-admin bootstrap ordering trap, the lab-session favicon CHP hack); the healthy backend; and the read-only Settings gap. `## Rebuild concept` proposes one TypeScript SPA owning the authenticated surface, served by the hub, consuming the existing APIs unchanged, executed as a strangler. It leads with `### Security model - hub as the trust boundary` (the governing constraint, added at the operator's direction): single trust boundary, SPA as just-another-client with no bypass, every mutation re-authorized server-side, capability-driven UI as rendering-not-authorization (render from capabilities, guard on the endpoint), JupyterHub scopes as the one authz model, lab access staying proxy/OAuth-mediated, groups/policy as a guard surface applied in `pre_spawn_hook`. Then feasibility (three layers - portal pages fully replaceable, protocol-bound pages with mandatory underlying flow, JupyterLab out of scope at the branding seam, pre-session pages kept server-rendered), the rebuild-vs-keep boundary, the stack (React + TypeScript, TanStack Query as the server-state layer, Vite bundle served by a hub handler, design tokens from the existing Stellars Sublime palette), three pillars (server-state cache replaces reloads, one push channel replaces six pollers, capability-driven UI generalises the registry), the modern/responsive/unified mapping, the strangler migration (groups first, admin last to kill the interception seam), and the risk (scope drift across the lab seam or into the handshake = forking the hub). Docs only; no code touched.

226. **Task [Extended] - Optimum Hub mock: IA redesign (navigate-to-nouns, role-aware)**: On `feature/new-frontend-mock` the operator interrogated the v1 mock's information architecture - why Servers and Activity are separate, why show the image, why no engagement signal, why uptime over time-left, why a Policies page, why Users/Groups are not under an admin section, why a CTA-shaped filter button - then layered four more asks: design each visual cue with its execution, split admin vs user home, make dashboard widgets mini-views that drill into a dedicated page, and borrow RustFS's user-config model<br>
    **Result**: Distilled all of it to one rule - navigate to nouns not views; one entity one place; separate watch (Operate) from administer (Administration); show only what drives a decision - and rebuilt from it. Every Overview widget is now a clickable mini-view linking to its full page. 253. **Task [Extended] - mock-antd: connect to real hub as parallel target portal** (v3.12.2): operator set the goal "portal connected, all actions work, real data + real operations, sign-in works" - turn the mocked `mock-antd` into the live target portal running alongside the existing JupyterHub for a later cut-over<br>
     **Result**: Backend mapping showed the gap was wiring, not new server code - the hub already ships the full `stellars-hub-services` REST API (activity, admin/groups + policy, session-info, manage-volumes, broadcast, credentials) plus standard JupyterHub endpoints. Built in five phases. **Client** (`services/hub/client.ts`): added `hubSend` (POST/PATCH/PUT/DELETE) carrying the `_xsrf` cookie as `X-XSRFToken`, `getCurrentUser`, plus `hubAuthGet`/`hubAuthForm` for NativeAuth's authorize/discard GET-toggles and change-password POSTs, and a 401/403->hub-login redirect; hub base is env-driven (`VITE_HUB_BASE`). **Auth/role** (`app/RoleContext.tsx`): live mode resolves identity from the session and derives admin from it, hiding the mock role-switch; `/login`+`/signup` hand off to the hub. **Reads** (`hub/liveSource.ts`): rewired to the real payload shapes - `/activity` is `{users:[...]}` indexed client-side and carries `is_authorized` + `time_remaining` + `activity_score`; session-info in seconds; groups `policy_summary` is a list (the old dict mapping was a bug). **Ops** (`services/ops.ts`, new): a mode-aware layer wiring every action - server start/stop/restart/extend, authorize/discard, user create/delete/admin/password, group CRUD/reorder/membership, tokens, broadcast, volume reset, bulk-add + credentials + client-side download. **Deploy**: an additive `nginx:alpine` (`deploy/compose.portal.yml`, `make build-live`/`deploy`) serving the build at `/portal` on the hub's Traefik host (same-origin so the cookie flows); hub image never rebuilt. Gotchas: the running deployment uses `base_url=/` + host-based routing (not the repo default `/jupyterhub`); the custom write handlers enforce Tornado XSRF **even under token auth** (proves the `X-XSRFToken` header is mandatory); pending (unauthorized) users have no JSON list endpoint so that panel reads empty in live; per-user GPU usage isn't collected. Verified end-to-end against the running hub via a throwaway admin (minted token -> create user -> set password -> real NativeAuth sign-in `302` -> cookie session rendered real identity/activity/11 groups -> group create+delete `200` via cookie+XSRF), then fully cleaned up. 254. **Task [Extended] - optimum-hub-web: hub-served portal replacing the stock UI, packaged standalone** (v3.12.2): operator set "replace the stock portal, build it in, admin+user log in, integrate elegantly" and renamed the artefact to `optimum-hub-web`<br>
     **Result**: The parallel `nginx` SPA at `/portal` (entry 253) was unusable - it "switched back and forth" - because JupyterHub 4's XSRF submit-token is hub-signed (`_get_signed_value_urlsafe`) and handed only to pages the hub renders (`window.jhdata.xsrf_token`), and the `_xsrf` cookie is `/hub/`-scoped so a `/portal` page can neither read it nor forge a valid one; every cookie-auth API GET `403`'d, looping the login gate. Fix: the hub serves the SPA at `/hub/portal` itself - a new `PortalHandler(BaseHandler)` renders a full-screen shell template (so `render_template` injects a valid `xsrf_token`, the same mechanism `page.html` uses for the stock admin React app) and serves the bundled assets file-or-shell from one `@web.authenticated` route. The SPA reads the token from `window.jhdata` and now sends `X-XSRFToken` on every call including `hubGet` (the actual GET-403 fix); `RoleContext` seeds name+admin from the injected `jhdata` so there's no "Connecting…" flash. Renamed `mock-antd/` -> `optimum-hub-web/` and folded a Python integration package (`optimum_hub_web/`) into it: one self-contained, hatchling-built wheel bundling the vite build (`static/`) plus the shell + `home`/`admin` templates; `portal_handlers()`/`PORTAL_URL`/`template_dir()` exported for config. Wired `config/jupyterhub_config.py`: `extra_handlers += portal_handlers()`, `template_dir()` prepended to `template_paths` (the `home.html`/`admin.html` redirect stubs shadow the stock 42K/50K enhanced pages), `default_url -> /hub/portal`, and `cleanup_servers=False` so the rebuild-restart leaves konrad/natalia labs running. `Dockerfile.jupyterhub` gained a `node:20` webbuilder stage feeding the Python builder's wheel; the target installs it alongside `stellars_hub_services`. Verified: `typecheck` clean, `build:hub` + default mock build both green (bases `/hub/portal/` vs `/`), wheel bundles UI+manifest+3 templates, host import smoke test passes (`PortalHandler` is `BaseHandler`, manifest resolves). Operator rebuilds/restarts when Natalia is off; this commit also lands the previously-uncommitted entry-253 live wiring.

267. **Task [Extended] - GPU-info sidecar replaces per-probe nvidia containers** (v3.12.2): operator asked whether the hub spins an nvidia container on every GPU read, then directed a sidecar redesign - lightweight FastAPI, separate package, dedicated network, one container for both detection and utilisation, robust vendor-neutral API for future amd/intel/applesilicon, and report processes to link load to a user<br>
     **Result**: Reads never spun a container (they hit a cache), but a 30s background tick spawned a fresh `nvidia/cuda` container (~1-3s) for utilisation plus one at startup for inventory - that churn is gone. New package `services/jupyterhub/gpuinfo-nvidia/`: a FastAPI app (`/health`, `/gpus`) over `nvidia.py`, which parses `nvidia-smi --query-gpu` (index/name/uuid/utilization/memory) and `--query-compute-apps` (per-GPU `{pid,name,used_memory_mb}` - the hook to attribute load to a user). Schema is vendor-neutral (pydantic `GpuReport`, `vendor` field, null-not-omitted) so future amd/intel/applesilicon sidecars implement the same contract; every probe degrades to `available:false`/`[]` rather than raising, and `/health` stays 200 even with no driver. Two-stage Dockerfile inside the package: build+test the wheel on slim Python (tests gate the build), then run on the CUDA base (`NVIDIA_IMAGE` build-arg) so nvidia-smi is present via the nvidia runtime. Hub side: new stdlib `gpu_client.py` (urllib, startup retry while unreachable, authoritative-empty otherwise); `gpu.py` enumerate and `gpu_cache.py` sampler both query the sidecar - one container now serves detection AND utilisation, no more `jupyterhub_gpu_enumerate`/`_util` spawns. `activity.py` carries `gpus[].processes` through. `config` reads `JUPYTERHUB_GPUINFO_URL` and calls `configure_gpu_cache(url)` before `resolve_gpu_mode()`. compose adds the `gpuinfo-nvidia` service (`runtime: nvidia`, no host port) on a dedicated `jupyterhub_gpuinfo` network whose name is env-driven (`JUPYTERHUB_GPUINFO_NETWORK_NAME`, default `jupyterhub-gpuinfo-network`) and baked into compose + `Dockerfile.jupyterhub` + `settings_dictionary.yml`; the hub joins it. Verified: 11 package tests + 518 hub-services tests + wheel build + `docker compose config` render + `tsc`. Needs operator rebuild (builds both images) + restart; GPU-less hosts drop the one service (hub degrades to GPU-off via the retry).

276. **Task [Extended] - optimum-hub: activity-score target normalisation + nine-task live-QA batch + old-portal prune** (v3.12.4): rapid live-testing session - operator fired ~10 issues then set the goal "finish all tasks, find root causes, update acceptance criteria"<br>
    **Result**: Headline: the activity meter under-reported (a full-time user showed 33%). Root cause - `ActivityMonitor.get_score` returned the raw decay-weighted active fraction (active vs ALL 24/7 samples), so 8h/24h = 33% was the mathematical ceiling; the original `activity.html` had normalised client-side (`activity_score / (targetHours/24)`) but the React portal dropped that step, and the documented `JUPYTERHUB_ACTIVITYMON_TARGET_HOURS` (8) was never wired into the scorer. Fix relocates the normalisation into `get_score` (`min(100, active_hours/target_hours*100)` via a shared `_weighted_active_fraction`) so every consumer agrees and 8h/day reads 100, 4h/day 50; added `get_avg_active_hours` (real, uncapped) exposed as `/activity` `activity_hours` and shown in the meter tooltip ("Active on average Nh/day over the last 3 days"), threaded through `liveSource`/`types`/`meters`/hero/Servers; 6 new monitor tests, 592 backend green. Other fixes: TTL extend bar now fills on click and holds until the refetched value lands (was a 1s timer firing before the 2-3s refetch, so it snapped back), duration 1s->3s; broadcast auto-close switched from on/off to 5 presets (30s/1m/10m/30m/1h, default 30s) sent as ms through the payload; `make increment_version` now sets the version absolutely across root + the three in-image wheels (`optimum-hub-web`, `stellars-hub-services`, `stellars-docker-proxy`; gpuinfo sidecar excluded), pulling drifted packages (hub-services was 3.8.0) back into lockstep; group import/export bundle restructured flat-config -> `group->policy[]->members` via `lib/policyShape.ts` (legacy flat still imports); the stale-name-in-list bug got the missing mount-time `['users']` invalidate in `Users.tsx` (mirrors `Home.tsx`); restart/stop modal now creeps the bar + rotates funny lines from the `loading-messages` npm package (no docker-specific package exists, used the maintained generic one). Old-portal prune: deleted the 4 dead page templates + the 4 unregistered `*PageHandler` classes (+ orphan `import os`, handler count 30->26) + the 368K `mock/` prototype; kept the still-live stock templates; held the auth/home shadowed templates for a rebuild-verified pass.     **Result**: #292 misread "1 bar red, 2 orange, 3 orange, 4 green, 5 green" as a per-POSITION gradient (red/orange/orange/green/green across the 5 segments); the operator meant a single uniform tone whose colour depends on the lit-bar COUNT - 1 lit bar pale red, 2-3 orange, 4-5 green, so a fuller meter reads greener. 296. **Task - optimum-hub: TTL extend boost animates to computed target, not 100%** (v4.0.4): operator live-QA - extending an already-banked session (56h +7h) animated the bar to 100% then flickered down to the real 63h<br>
    **Result**: The staged-extend animation hard-coded the optimistic fill to 100% (`shownPct = boost ? 100 : pct`) - correct under the old model where above-base time pinned at 100%, but the 2026-06-17 rework made the extended bar drain against the ceiling, so the boost overshot to full then snapped down to the real ceiling-scaled % when the refetch landed. Factored the two-phase pct into `pctFor(min)` and at extend click captured `boostPct = pctFor(min(ceiling, timeLeft + addedHours))`, the true post-extend target; `shownPct = boost ? boostPct : pct`. The ceiling is invariant across an extend so the landed % equals `boostPct` - the bar grows smoothly (78%->87.5% here) with no overshoot or snap. tsc + eslint + build:hub green; `acc-crit-ttl-extend-animation` + `acc-crit-ttl-progress-bar` matrices updated.

297. **Task [Extended] - optimum-hub: lightweight activity-gated container-stats cache (kills the /activity 5-6s lag)** (v4.0.4): operator live-QA - the portal's activity map only refreshed ~5-6s after switching to a portal page; the hub must keep it fresh without polling idle containers<br>
    **Result**: `/activity` did a synchronous `asyncio.gather(get_container_stats_async ...)` over every active user on the request path - live `docker stats` (~1-2s/container, 4-worker pool) held the response 5-6s and nothing refreshed between requests. Moved stats off the request path into a warm snapshot (`container_stats_cache.py`): `/activity` now reads `get_container_stats_with_refresh(active_encoded)` non-blocking and returns instantly, while status stays request-fresh from `spawner.last_activity` (no Docker). Per the operator's two follow-up steers - "lightweight" then "trigger only when a container gives an active signal" - the refresh is LAZY (no always-on `PeriodicCallback`; fires only when `/activity` is polled and the snapshot is stale, at most once per interval) and samples ONLY recently-active users (reusing the platform's existing `recently_active`/`last_activity` signal rather than a second threshold); idle-but-running containers keep their last value and are never polled, and an all-idle deployment makes zero docker calls (empty active set -> no submit, no `/containers/json`). Factored `stats_from_container` in `docker_utils` as the single stats-math source shared by the ad-hoc `get_container_stats` and the cache. Interval env `JUPYTERHUB_ACTIVITYMON_STATS_INTERVAL` (default 10s). Dropped the originally-planned always-on refresher and the secondary frontend poll as too heavy for the lightweight goal. New `acc-crit-activity-map-freshness.md` + `test_container_stats_cache.py` (10 tests: shared stats math limited/unlimited/error, snapshot staleness, refresh-trigger gating - no real Docker). `make test` 621 + 63 green; needs an operator rebuild to activate.

304. **Task - optimum-hub: first live functional run exposes + fixes a rename NO_VALUE bug** (v4.0.4): operator - execute all functional tests; the run surfaced a real failure plus backend log spam on every user create<br>
    **Result**: Ran `make test-functional` against the matching `:latest` (built 11:04, just after the rename/Roles commit) - the first true end-to-end run of the rename/Roles/nav wave: 22 passed, 1 failed in 27s, exposing two real defects. (a) `events.py::sync_nativeauth_on_rename` guarded only `oldvalue is None`, but the INITIAL name-set (user creation) passes SQLAlchemy's `NO_VALUE` sentinel - so every create spammed the hub log (`type 'LoaderCallableStatus' is not supported`; the sentinel can't bind into the username lookups) AND recorded a bogus "renamed <sentinel> to <name>" event. Fixed the guard to `if not isinstance(oldvalue, str) or oldvalue == value`, covering None / NO_VALUE / no-op uniformly. (b) `test_rename_user_flow` asserted the Rename button enabled before typing, but it is correctly disabled while the name is unchanged - reordered to fill-then-assert (plus a disabled-on-load assertion).     **Result**: New `docs/gpuinfo-api.md` - the sidecar contract (`GET /health`, `GET /gpus`), the `Gpu`/`GpuReport`/`Health` schema with units-in-names + null-not-omitted semantics, and the hub-side consumption path (`gpu_client` urllib, `gpu.py` detection modes 0/1/2, `gpu_cache` 30s warm snapshot, `gpuinfo_sidecar` recreate-fresh lifecycle, env vars). 316. **Task [Extended] - CPU dashboard discrepancy root-cause + resource-bar colour fix** (v4.0.5): operator - konrad shows 93% Server CPU while Host CPU reads 7%, and a ~93% bar stays pale orange instead of red<br>
    **Result**: The 93%-vs-7% split is not a bug - the two widgets use different denominators. The per-server Server Status bar is usage over that server's *assigned* cores (`cpuBarPct = cpu_percent / cpu_cores`, `liveSource.ts`); konrad's container is CPU-limited (~2 cores via his group's CPU policy -> `cpu_cores≈2`, `cpu_cores_limited`), so 93% means he is saturating his cap. Host Status divides summed cores-used by the host core count (`coresUsed / hostCores`), so the same ~1.86 cores read 7% of a ~26-core host - `0.93x2 ≈ 1.86 ≈ 0.07x26`, and `cpu_percent` (docker `(cpu_delta/system_delta)*online_cpus*100`) is correct. The real signal: konrad throttled to ~2 cores while the host idles ~93%, a group CPU-limit config matter, not code - no arithmetic fault in `docker_utils.stats_from_container` or the activity assembly. Separately fixed a genuine bug: `barColor()` (`meters.tsx`) ramped warning->danger linearly across 75-100%, leaving a 93% bar only 72% red (pale orange); it now saturates to full `--color-danger` at >=90% and steepens 75-90, so a near-full bar reads strong red. Shared by every resource bar (CPU/memory, server/host); updated `acc-crit-resource-bars.md`; needs a portal rebuild to surface live.

317. **Task [Extended] - hub address recovery: stop hardcoding the hostname (gethostname + 0.0.0.0)** (v4.0.5): operator - the `duoptimum-hub` rename kept crash-looping on `socket.gaierror` at hub bind; recover to a working state and record why hardcoding the hostname is the trap<br>
    **Result**: The recurring boot crash (`http_server.listen(port, address=ip)` -> `getaddrinfo` -> `gaierror: Name or service not known`) came from `config` hardcoding `c.JupyterHub.hub_ip` / `hub_connect_url` to the compose SERVICE name (`duoptimumhub`, then `duoptimum-hub`): that name resolves only once the rename is consistent across every file, so any partial rename strands the hub at bind time. Patching around it (binding `hub_ip="0.0.0.0"` plus a DNS wait-loop) overreached and was rejected; recovered cleanly with `git reset --hard` to the last good commit (`a11ec1c`), then re-applied minimally. The durable fix is to NOT hardcode the hostname at all: `hub_ip="0.0.0.0"` (bind/listen on all interfaces - a pure listen address with zero name resolution, so it can never `gaierror`) and `hub_connect_url = f'http://{socket.gethostname()}:8080' + prefix + '/hub'`, where `gethostname()` returns whatever Docker set the container HOSTNAME to, read at runtime - a service or image rename never touches `config` again. A probe corrected a wrong assumption: a compose `hostname:` IS registered in Docker's embedded DNS for peers (verified with `getent hosts` from a peer lab), so `hostname: jupyterhub` both makes `gethostname()` return `jupyterhub` and lets spawned labs reach the hub at that stable, brand-neutral name regardless of the service name. Renamed the compose service/container/image `duoptimumhub` -> `duoptimum-hub`, rebuilt `stellars/duoptimum-hub:latest` (`make build NO_VERSION_INCREMENT=1`, no version bump). Minimised the wrapper `compose_override.yml` to deltas-only - dropped everything inherited from the base (image, ports, volumes, networks, watchtower, redundant env) and, crucially, overwrote the base label KEY `duoptimumhub-rtr` IN PLACE (host rule + `middlewares=duoptimumhub-ratelimit`) instead of adding a parallel `duoptimum-hub-rtr`, which had left the base `hub-alias-redirect` live (302 `/hub/*` -> `/jupyterhub/*` -> 404). Deployed live and verified: hub healthy, `hostname=jupyterhub`, portal at `/hub/home`, existing labs (konrad, natalia) reconnect; then stopped with `down` (keeps the spawned labs - they are orphans, not declared services). Lesson: never hardcode the hub hostname in `config` - bind `0.0.0.0`, advertise `socket.gethostname()`.

320. **Task [Extended] - notifications: "Never" auto-close default, type cleanup, self-healing sent-history store** (v4.0.5): operator - default auto-close to "Never", drop the 'default' type (default 'info'), the sent-notifications list never updated, make the store self-healing + log it, and unit-test the types<br>
    **Result**: Composer (`Notifications.tsx`): added a "Never" auto-close option (value 0, sent as `autoClose:false`) and made it the default (was 30s); removed 'default' from the type Select and defaulted to 'info'. Canonicalised the types backend-side as `NOTIFICATION_TYPES = (info, success, warning, error, in-progress)` in `handlers/notifications.py` - the single source of truth the handler validates against (now rejects 'default' and anything else). Root-caused "the sent list never updates": live `getSentNotifications` was hardcoded `[]` ("no backend store yet"), so "Past Notifications" was always empty on the hub - the broadcast only recorded an HTML event string, which cannot reconstruct the message/type/delivered columns. Built a dedicated store `sent_notification_log.py` (bounded SQLite, mirrors `event_log`/`groups_config`): the broadcast handler now `record_sent_notification(message, variant, successful, total)`, a new admin-only `SentNotificationsDataHandler` serves `GET /api/notifications/sent`, and the live source reads it (degrades to empty on failure). Per operator the store self-heals at boot: `prepare()` (called after `register_events()` in `config`) creates the table when the /data DB lacks it (fresh or inherited from an older deploy) and rebuilds it when an inherited table carries a stale schema (missing columns), logging every create/repair to `jupyterhub.sent_notification_log` and staying silent when the schema is good - never raising into boot. Unit tests `test_sent_notification_log.py` cover record/recent (portal row shape), pruning, the best-effort helper, both self-heal paths (create + stale-table rebuild, asserting the log lines) and that every sent type round-trips while the canonical set excludes 'default'; `test_imports` handler count 28 -> 29. Clarified the "stopped" worry: `NotificationPill` maps `default` -> a gray *tone class* (not a visible type), kept for historical rows. Also fixed the wrapper `compose_override.yml`: dropped the `traefik ./certs:/certs` direct mount so Traefik reads the hub-provisioned `jupyterhub_certs` volume (the hub does operator-or-auto from `/user-certs` per `00_provision_certificates.sh`), validated via rendered `docker compose config`. `make test` 640 pass; `tsc` + `eslint` clean; pends a rebuild to bake.
